Miracles Are Not Magic: Refuting the Confusion
Refutation of the claim that miracles are merely magic or sleight of hand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinctions between miracles, magic, and sleight of hand, and why miracles cannot be reduced to sorcery.

Core Idea
Miracles strengthen under scrutiny; magic and trickery dissolve.

Some might argue that since both miracles and magic involve extraordinary events, they are essentially the same. This lesson tackles that claim head-on. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, refutes this confusion by showing that miracles, magic, and jugglery differ in their nature, origin, and effects. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for a sound Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you analyze.
The text ends abruptly; the argument is complete enough for our purpose.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage discusses miracles (المعجزة), magic (السحر), and jugglery/trickery (الشعبذة/المخرفة). Notice how each is defined and contrasted.
Jugglery is based on illusion, magic on polytheism, miracles on divine power.
3
Analyze the contrasts
Focus on the three contrasts: (1) effect upon investigation, (2) source/practitioners, (3) associated conditions. These are the core of the refutation.
The author uses these contrasts to show the objection is corrupt speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة والرد عليها: وأما من يزعم أن قلب العادة والطبيعة جائز، غير أن ذلك أيضا في مقدور السحرة والمشعبذة. فكلام فاسد، إذ المشعبذة والمخرفة يزداد ضعفا واضمحلالا لدى البحث عنهما والتأمل فيهما، إذ المخرفة تمويه محض، والشعبذة مبنية على سفل أعين الناظرين بشيء ثم إخراج غيره وعلى المهارة في خفة اليد. والمعجزة تزداد عند البحث والتأمل وكادة وعلى مر الأيام ثباتا ودواما. والسحر من علائق الكلمات المؤلفة من الشرك الخالص والكفر المحض والتعمد لتفخيم الشياطين. ثم في الأعم الأغلب يظهر على أيدي الحيض من النساء وذوي القذارة والنجاسة من الرجال، في أوقات ومواضع لا يجري فيها ذكر الله تعالى، وإذا وافقه
A specious argument and its refutation: As for the one who claims that the violation of custom and nature is permissible, but that also lies within the power of sorcerers and jugglers: this is corrupt speech. For jugglers and tricksters increase in weakness and dissolution upon investigation and reflection, because trickery is pure illusion, and jugglery is based on causing the eyes of the onlookers to look down at something and then bringing out something else, and on skill in the lightness of hand. The miracle increases upon investigation and reflection and strength, and over the course of days, in steadfastness and permanence. And magic consists of attachments of words composed of pure polytheism and sheer disbelief, and deliberate glorification of devils. Then, in most cases, it appears at the hands of menstruating women and those men who are filthy and impure, at times and places where the remembrance of God is not mentioned. And if it agrees...
Source pages p. 705

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection: some might say that violation of natural laws (miracles) are possible, but they are also done by sorcerers and jugglers. The author dismisses this as corrupt speech. He distinguishes miracles from trickery and magic: jugglery (الشعبذة) and trickery (المخرفة) are based on illusion and sleight of hand, and they weaken under scrutiny. Miracles, by contrast, increase in strength and permanence when investigated. Magic (السحر) involves words of polytheism and disbelief, glorifying devils, and is typically performed by impure individuals in impure conditions, without remembrance of God. Thus, miracles are fundamentally different from magic and cannot be attributed to sorcerers.

Key Terms
المعجزة
السحر
الشعبذة
المخرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think miracles and magic are the same because both involve extraordinary events.
Correction: They differ fundamentally in origin (divine vs. satanic), effect (permanent vs. illusory), and associated practices (pure vs. impure).

Checkpoint
According to the author, how does a miracle differ from jugglery and trickery?
A) Miracles are performed by impure individuals.
B) Miracles increase in strength upon investigation, while trickery weakens.
C) Miracles involve sleight of hand.
D) Miracles are based on polytheistic words.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine signs that increase in strength when examined, whereas magic and jugglery are based on illusion and disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a claim that seems extraordinary—whether in religion or in daily life—do you instinctively celebrate it, or do you test it? What does your response reveal about your attachment to truth over spectacle?
?
The passage teaches that magic thrives in environments devoid of God's remembrance. Where in your own life—your habits, your media consumption, your conversations—have you allowed a 'remembrance-free' zone to take root? What will you do to change that this week?
?
If a miracle strengthens under scrutiny, and your faith must withstand doubts and tests, are you actively exposing your beliefs to honest investigation? Or are you hiding behind comfortable blindness? Commit to one way you will deliberately test the strength of your faith today.

Miracles
intermediate
8 min
Distinguishing Miracles from Sorcery and Jugglery
Nasafi refutes the claim that miracles are the same as sorcery and jugglery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi distinguishes miracles from sorcery and jugglery through three main arguments: the nature of the acts, the character of the doer, and divine intervention.

Core Idea
Miracles and sorcery differ in source, context, and permanence.

A common objection against prophethood is that miracles are no different from the tricks of sorcerers and jugglers. Nasafi takes this objection head-on, showing that careful investigation reveals fundamental differences. In this passage, he refutes the claim by examining the nature of jugglery, sorcery, and miracles, as well as the character of those who perform them, and then highlights how God Himself preserves the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection: the opponent claims that breaking custom is possible for both prophets and sorcerers, implying no distinction.
2
See Nasafi's first refutation
Notice how jugglery weakens under scrutiny while miracles grow firmer. This shows a difference in intrinsic nature.
3
See the second refutation
Compare the contexts of sorcery (polytheism, impurity) with those of prophethood (remembrance of God, purity). The character of the doer differs completely.
4
Understand the third refutation
Nasafi argues that if a sorcerer claimed prophethood and tried to produce a miracle, God would prevent him. Divine wisdom maintains the distinction.
This reinforces the unique status of miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة والرد عليها] وأما من يزعم أن قلب العادة والطبيعة جائز، غير أن ذلك أيضا في مقدور السحرة والمشعبذة. فكلام فاسد، إذ المشعبذة والمخرفة يزداد ضعفًا واضمحلالاً لدى البحث عنهما والتأمل فيهما، إذ المخرفة تمويه محض، والشعبذة مبنية على سفل أعين الناظرين بشيء ثم إخراج غيره وعلى المهارة في خفة اليد. والمعجزة تزداد عند البحث والتأمل وكادة () وعلى مر الأيام ثباتاً ودواما. والسحر من علائق الكلمات المؤلفة من الشرك الخالص والكفر المحض والتعمد لتفخيم الشياطين. ثم في الأعم الأغلب يظهر على أيدي الحيض من النساء وذوي القذارة والنجاسة من الرجال، في أوقات ومواضع لا يجري فيها ذكر الله تعالى، وإذا وافقه شيء من ذكر الله تعالى ينمحق ويضمحل. ولهذا يكون نفوذه في بلاد الشرك وعبادة الأصنام أشد وأبلغ، وهذا لأن ذلك يظهر بمعونة الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة فلابد من تقرب ممن يطلب منهم العناية إليهم بما ذكرنا من التباعد عن ذكر الله تعالى وطاعته ومباشرة الأعمال الخبيثة وملامسة الأشياء المستقذرة، وحال الأنبياء عليهم السلام كانت في نهاية المخالفة من هذه الأحوال، إذ هم المواظبون على ذكر الله تعالى المداومون على جميع أنواع القرب، والموصوفون بالتطهر عن النجاسات والأقذار. فتمتاز المعجز عن السحر بأحوال الآتي بهما المكتسب لهما، على أنا بينا أن الله تعالى هو الذي يظهر المعجزة عقيب الدعوى على يد مدعي النبوة تأكيدًا لدعوته وتصديقًا له في دعواه الرسالة، فلو ادعى أحد من المشعبذة والسحرة النبوة، وأراد إيجاد ما هو ناقض العادة ليكون دلالة له على صدق مقالته لأعجزه الله تعالى عن إظهار ناقض للعادة وأبطل سحره وكيده في هذه الحالة، صيانة لحججه عن أن يعارضها باطل أو يقاومها فاسد، وهذا لما مر أن لابد في حق الحكمة من إثبات تفرقة الحق والباطل، ودفع ما يوجب التسوية بينهما، وإثبات القدرة للصانع على ذلك، وامتناع تعجيزه ذلك على نحو ما قررنا، والله ولي التوفيق.
[Objection and its refutation] As for one who claims that the changing of custom and nature is permissible, but that this is also within the capacity of sorcerers and jugglers (mushʿabidha): it is corrupt speech. For juggling and deception (mukharrafa) increase in weakness and dissolution upon investigation and reflection about them, since deception (mukharrafa) is pure delusion, and juggling is based on distracting the eyes of the viewers with something and then bringing out another, and on skill in manual dexterity. The miracle (muʿjiza) increases upon investigation and reflection and strengthening and over days in firmness and permanence. Sorcery (siḥr) is among the attachments of words composed of pure polytheism and absolute disbelief and intentional magnifying of devils. Then, in the vast majority of cases, it appears at the hands of menstruating women and those possessing filth and impurity among men, at times and places where the remembrance of God Most High does not occur, and if it coincides with something of the remembrance of God Most High, it decays and vanishes. Therefore its influence is stronger and more effective in lands of polytheism and idol worship, and this is because it appears with the help of devils and evil spirits, so it necessitates drawing near to those who seek their attention by what we mentioned of distance from the remembrance of God Most High and His obedience, and engaging in evil deeds and touching impure things. The condition of the prophets, peace be upon them, was in extreme opposition to these states, for they are the constant in remembrance of God Most High, the persistent in all types of acts of devotion, and described as purified from impurities and filth. So the miracle is distinguished from sorcery by the states of those who bring them and acquire them, in addition to the fact that We have clarified that God Most High is the one who manifests the miracle after the claim at the hand of the claimant of prophethood, as a confirmation of his call and a verification of his claim of messengerhood. So if any of the jugglers or sorcerers claimed prophethood and wanted to produce something that breaks custom to be an evidence for the truth of his statement, God Most High would incapacitate him from manifesting a breaker of custom and would nullify his sorcery and his plot in that situation, as a protection of His proofs from being opposed by falsehood or resisted by corruption. And this is due to what has passed: that in the interest of wisdom (ḥikma) it is necessary to establish a distinction between truth and falsehood, and to repel what necessitates equality between them, and to establish the power (qudra) of the Maker over that, and the impossibility of His being incapacitated regarding that, in the manner we have explained. And God is the Possessor of success.
Source pages p. 705

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer: someone claims that miracles are possible but so are acts of sorcerers and jugglers, implying no distinction. Nasafi refutes this. First, he states that jugglers' acts weaken under scrutiny because they rely on deception and sleight of hand, while miracles become stronger and more established with investigation and time. Sorcery, he explains, is based on polytheistic words and devil-worship, often performed by impure individuals in places devoid of God's remembrance. In contrast, prophets are constant in worship and purity. Thus, miracles are distinguished by the character of the performer. Furthermore, God Himself intervenes: He causes the miracle to appear exactly after the prophetic claim, and if a sorcerer attempted to claim prophethood and produce a miracle, God would prevent him, preserving the distinction between truth and falsehood. This is necessary for divine wisdom to maintain a difference between the truthful and the false.

Key Terms
معجزة
سحر
شعبذة
مخرفة
قدرة
حكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are no different from sorcery or jugglery.
Correction: Nasafi shows they differ in nature (miracles are permanent, jugglery is deceptive), in the character of the doer (prophets are pure, sorcerers impure), and in divine intervention (God prevents sorcerers from producing miracles when claiming prophethood).

Checkpoint

A) It becomes stronger.
B) It increases in firmness.
C) It weakens and dissolves.
D) It remains the same.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are fundamentally distinct from sorcery and jugglery in their nature, context, and divine preservation.

?
Nasafi highlights that sorcerers distance themselves from God’s remembrance and engage in impurity to gain power. How can you realign these pursuits with constant dhikr and purity of intention?
?

The Magnet Example: God's Protection of Miracles
Nasafi uses a magnet example to illustrate God's protection of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God actively safeguards the integrity of miracles by disabling natural causes that could be used by false claimants.

Core Idea
God disables natural causes to preserve the distinctiveness of true miracles.

In this passage, al-Nasafi presents a vivid hypothetical scenario to illustrate a key theological principle: God actively safeguards the signs of prophethood from being confused with ordinary natural events. Through the example of a magnet, he shows that God would intervene to prevent a false claimant from using a natural property as a miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to understand the scenario.
Notice the authoritative tone: 'our masters said'.
2
Identify the hypothetical scenario
A person obtains a magnet, goes to a region ignorant of its property, claims prophethood, and uses iron attraction as proof.
The magnet's property is natural, not miraculous.
3
Understand God's action
God nullifies the proof by removing the magnetic property at that moment.
This shows divine intervention to protect the truth.
4
Reflect on the purpose
God's action protects the evidences of prophethood from doubt and confusion, preserving the purpose of sending messengers.
Without such protection, true prophethood could be doubted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قال مشايخنا إن من ظفر بحجر المغناطيس ثم أتى ناحية من آفاق الأرض، لم يعلم أهلها بما هو من خاصية المغناطيس من جذب الفولاذ ثم ادعى الرسالة، وجعل حجة دعواه وآية صدقه القدرة على جذب الحديد، أبطل الله تعالى حجته وسلب تلك الخاصية عن ذلك الحجر في تلك الحال، صيانة لدلائل النبوة عن أن يدخلها شائبة التشكيك أو يلحقها بوجه من الوجوه نقص أو ضعف، إذ لو أبقى ذلك على حاله لأدى إلى إلتباس حاله بحال الصادقين، ولكان ذلك مدعاة للشك في النبوات ورافعاً للثقة، وذلك نقض للغرض من إرسال الرسل وإنزال الكتب.
And this is why our masters (mashāyikh) said: If someone obtained a magnet, then came to a region of the earth whose inhabitants were unaware of the property of the magnet in attracting iron, and then claimed prophethood, making his evidence for his claim and the sign of his truthfulness his ability to attract iron, God Most High would nullify his proof and remove that property from the stone at that moment, as a protection of the evidences of prophethood from being entered by any blemish of doubt or from being overtaken in any manner by deficiency or weakness. For if He allowed it to remain as it was, it would lead to confusion between his situation and the situation of the truthful ones, and that would be a cause for doubt in prophethood and a removal of confidence, and that is a violation of the purpose of sending messengers and revealing books.
Source pages p. 706

Commentary
This passage provides an example from the earlier masters (مشايخنا) to illustrate God's protection of miracles. The scenario: a person obtains a magnet, which has the natural property of attracting iron. He goes to a place where people do not know this property, claims prophethood, and presents the attraction of iron as his miracle. God would then remove that property from the magnet at that moment, thus preventing the false claim from being accepted. The reason is to protect the proofs of prophethood from any confusion with sorcery or natural phenomena. If God allowed such a trick to succeed, it would create doubt and undermine confidence in true prophets, defeating the purpose of sending messengers and scriptures. This reinforces the idea that God actively safeguards the distinctiveness of genuine miracles.

Key Terms
حجر المغناطيس (magnet stone)
خاصية (property)
دلائل النبوة (evidences of prophethood)
تشكيك (causing doubt)
نقض الغرض (violation of purpose)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a natural phenomenon like magnetism could be used by a false prophet as a genuine miracle.
Correction: Nasafi shows that God would disable the natural property, preventing it from serving as a proof for a false claim.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would God do if a person used a magnet to claim prophethood?
A) Allow the magnet to attract iron as a miracle.
B) Destroy the magnet.
C) Remove the attracting property from the magnet at that moment.
D) Cause the person to fail in his claim.

Key Takeaway
God actively protects the uniqueness of prophetic miracles by disabling natural causes that could be mistaken for them.

?
When you hear about false prophets or deceptive claims, do you ever feel doubt creep in? How does this passage remind you that Allah actively guards the distinction between truth and falsehood, and what assurance does that give you personally?

Distinguishing Miracles from Magic and Divine Protection
Explaining the distinction between miracles and magic with divine protection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles are distinguished from magic through their source and context, and how God protects His proofs from being counterfeited.

Core Idea
Miracles are divine, magic is demonic; God prevents false claimants from producing miracles.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi establishes the essential difference between the miracles of prophets and the magic of sorcerers. It explains that miracles come from God as confirmation of prophethood, while magic relies on demonic assistance. The author also shows how God protects His proofs by disabling any attempt to produce a counterfeit miracle, using the concrete example of a loadstone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then follow with the English translation. Notice the flow from describing magic to contrasting prophets, then to the distinction and the loadstone example.
2
Contrast prophets and sorcerers
Identify how the author contrasts the states of prophets (constant remembrance of Allah, purity) with sorcerers (avoidance of Allah, evil deeds). Understand that this contrast is part of the distinction.
Prophets are devoted to God; sorcerers rely on devils.
3
Analyze the loadstone example
Consider the hypothetical: a person uses a loadstone's natural property to claim prophethood. The author says God would nullify that property. Reflect on why this is necessary for protecting divine proofs.
This shows God actively prevents false miracles.
4
Reflect on the argument
Connect the loadstone example to the overarching principle: God must distinguish truth from falsehood and cannot be incapacitated. Recognize that obvious miracles (like turning a staff into a snake) are beyond human power and thus cannot be opposed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيء من ذكر الله تعالى ينمحق ويضمحل. ولهذا يكون نفوذه في بلاد الشرك وعبادة الأصنام أشد وأبلغ، وهذا لأن ذلك يظهر بمعونة الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة فلابد من تقرب ممن يطلب منهم العناية إليهم بما ذكرنا من التباعد عن ذكر الله تعالى وطاعته ومباشرة الأعمال الخبيثة وملامسة الأشياء المستقذرة، وحال الأنبياء عليهم السلام كانت في نهاية المخالفة من هذه الأحوال، إذ هم المواظبون على ذكر الله تعالى المداومون على جميع أنواع القرب، والموصوفون بالتطهر عن النجاسات والأقذار. فتمتاز المعجز عن السحر بأحوال الآتي بهما المكتسب لهما، على أنا بينا أن الله تعالى هو الذي يظهر المعجزة عقيب الدعوى على يد مدعي النبوة تأكيدًا لدعوته وتصديقًا له في دعواه الرسالة، فلو ادعى أحد من المشعبذة والسحرة النبوة، وأراد إيجاد ما هو ناقض العادة ليكون دلالة له على صدق مقالته لأعجزه الله تعالى عن إظهار ناقض للعادة وأبطل سحره وكيده في هذه الحالة، صيانة لحججه عن أن يعارضها باطل أو يقاومها فاسد، وهذا لما مر أن لابد في حق الحكمة من إثبات تفرقة الحق والباطل، ودفع ما يوجب التسوية بينهما، وإثبات القدرة للصانع على ذلك، وامتناع تعجيزه ذلك على نحو ما قررنا، والله ولي التوفيق. ولهذا قال مشايخنا إن من ظفر بحجر المغناطيس ثم أتى ناحية من آفاق الأرض، لم يعلم أهلها بما هو من خاصية المغناطيس من جذب الفولاذ ثم ادعى الرسالة، وجعل حجة دعواه وآية صدقه القدرة على جذب الحديد، أبطل الله تلك الخاصية عن المغناطيس، صيانة لحججه عن المعارضة، وحفظًا لدينه الحق عن أن يقاومه باطل، وبالله التوفيق. على أنه لا ريب لأحد لم يكن من شأنه العناد والمكابرة أن قلب العصا حية، وفلق البحر، وإحياء الموتى، وشق القمر، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع، وغير ذلك من هذه المعجزات الحسية، ليست من أنواع ما يدخل تحت مقدور أحد غير الله تعالى، وقد لا يخطر جواز ذلك من غير الله تعالى على قلب عاقل البتة، فلا يتمكن إذا فيه المعارضة.
Something of the remembrance of God Almighty fades and vanishes. Therefore its influence in the lands of polytheism and idol worship is more severe and greater, and that is because it appears with the help of devils and evil spirits, so they must draw near to those from whom they seek assistance by what we mentioned of distancing from the remembrance of God Almighty and His obedience, and undertaking evil deeds and touching impure things. The state of the prophets, peace be upon them, was at the utmost opposition to these states, as they are persistent in the remembrance of God Almighty, constant in all types of acts of worship, and described as purified from impurities and filth. Thus the miracle is distinguished from magic by the states of the one who brings them and acquires them. Moreover, we have explained that God Almighty is the One who manifests the miracle following the claim upon the hand of the claimant of prophethood as confirmation of his call and verification of his claim of messengership. So if any of the sorcerers and magicians were to claim prophethood and intend to produce something that breaks custom to be a proof of the truth of his statement, God Almighty would incapacitate him from manifesting a custom-breaker and would nullify his magic and cunning in that situation, as protection for His proofs from being opposed by falsehood or resisted by corruption. And this is because, as has passed, it is necessary for wisdom to establish a distinction between truth and falsehood, and to repel what necessitates equality between them, and to establish the power of the Maker over that, and the impossibility of Him being incapacitated from that, in the manner we have established. And God is the Grantor of success. For this reason our scholars said: If someone obtains a loadstone, then goes to a region of the earth whose inhabitants do not know the property of the loadstone in attracting iron, then claims prophethood and makes his proof of his claim and the sign of his truthfulness the ability to attract iron, God would nullify that property from the loadstone, as protection for His proofs from opposition, and safeguard for His true religion from being resisted by falsehood. And God grants success. Moreover, there is no doubt for anyone not given to stubbornness and obstinacy that the turning of the staff into a serpent, the splitting of the sea, the reviving of the dead, the splitting of the moon, the gushing of water from between the fingers, and other such sensory miracles are not of the types that fall under the power of anyone other than God Almighty, and the possibility of that from other than God never occurs to the heart of a rational person at all. Thus opposition to them is not possible.
Source pages p. 706

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanation and proof of the distinction between miracles and magic, and how God protects His proofs. The author begins by describing how sorcery operates through avoidance of God’s remembrance and association with devils, in contrast to the prophets who are always devoted to God and pure. The key difference is that miracles are performed by God following a claim of prophethood, whereas magic is acquired through human effort with demonic aid. If a magician were to claim prophethood and attempt a miracle, God would prevent him from succeeding. This is necessary to maintain the distinction between truth and falsehood. The author then gives the example of a loadstone: if someone used its natural property to attract iron as a proof of prophethood, God would disable that property so the claim would fail. Finally, he argues that obvious miracles like turning a staff into a serpent are beyond any human power and cannot be opposed.

سحر
مشعبذة
ناقض العادة
حجر المغناطيس
شيطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think miracles are just a more advanced form of magic.
Correction: This passage shows the essential difference: miracles are divine acts performed by God through prophets, while magic relies on demonic aid and is acquired through impure practices. Moreover, God protects His proofs by preventing false claimants from producing miracles.

Checkpoint

B) That God can disable natural properties to prevent false miracles.
C) That magicians can also perform miracles.
D) That prophets used stones to prove their prophethood.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine acts confirming prophethood, while magic is demonic; God actively protects His proofs by disabling any attempt to counterfeit a miracle.

Miracles Cannot Be Earned: Refuting the Training Doubt
The author refutes the claim that anyone can produce a miracle through training and the example of Zarathustra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that miracles can be produced by anyone through training, using the prophets' public lives and the example of Zarathustra.

Core Idea
Prophets are known to be untrained; their miracles are true signs, not earned skills.

This passage tackles a common objection: perhaps anyone can produce a miracle with enough effort. The author counters by noting that prophets were observed from birth to their claim, and no one saw them train. He also addresses the counterexample of Zarathustra, showing that not every custom-breaking act is a genuine miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the opening phrase 'شبهة والرد عليها' which sets up the doubt. The objector claims that miracles are achievable through exertion and that prophets haven't tested everyone's abilities.
The objection is in the first sentence up to 'قوى الجميع'.
2
Understand the first refutation
The author replies that even if we accept the possibility, the prophets had no exertion, training, or habit in such acts. Their acts break the normal course of things, making them true miracles.
Key terms: اجتهاد, تدرب, اعتياد.
3
Examine the second refutation: community testimony
The author emphasizes that the prophets' communities witnessed their entire lives—from birth to adulthood—and never saw them engage in any practice or associate with practitioners. This proves they did not train secretly.
The phrase 'عاينوا أحوالهم وشاهدوا منذ ولدوا' highlights the public nature of their lives.
4
Analyze the Zarathustra counterexample
If someone objects using Zarathustra's apparent miracle, the author implies that it was not a genuine miracle (perhaps lacking divine confirmation), so it doesn't disprove the rule.
The passage ends with 'فكذا ما أنتم تدعونه' meaning 'so likewise what you claim is not a proof.'
5
Summarize the author's argument
Reflect on why the author's reasoning is effective: miracles are not earned skills but divine signs; prophets are publicly known to be untrained; custom-breaking acts from false claimants are not true miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة والرد عليها وبهذا كله يبطل قول من يقول: إن قلب العادة الذي أتى به مدعي الرسالة مما يمكن تحصيله لمن له في نوعه تكلف واجتهاد والمدعون ما امتحنوا قوى الجميع. على أنا نقول لهم: لو ساعدناكم لكان وجوده مما لم يكن له بذلك اجتهاد وتدرب واعتياد نقضا للمادة، فيكون دليلاً لصحة دعواهم، والمدعون للرسالة له لم يكن لهم بذلك اجتهاد ولا اعتياد عرف ذلك منهم قومهم الذين نشأوا هم بين أظهرهم، إذ عاينوا أحوالهم وشاهدوا منذ ولدوا إلى أن كبروا وادعوا ما ادعوا من الرسالة، فلم يروهم اشتغلوا بشيء من ذلك، ولا اعتادوا تعاطيه، ولا صحبوا من له بذلك علم واعتياد، وخروج ذلك على أيدي مثلهم ناقض للعادة، فكان معجزة كافية والله الموفق. وإن قابلوا ذلك بما ظهر من الناقض للعادة على يدي زرادشت ولم يكن ذلك علمًا لصحة دعواه فكذا ما أنتم تدعونه.
A doubt and its refutation: And by all this, the statement of those who say is invalidated: 'The breaking of custom brought by the claimant of messengership is something that can be obtained by anyone who puts effort and exertion into its type, and the claimants have not tested the powers of everyone.' Rather, we say to them: Even if we agreed with you, its existence would be such that he had no exertion, training, or habit in it—a breaking of the material—so it would be a proof of the truth of their claim. And the claimants of messengership had no exertion or habit in that, as their people knew, who grew up among them, since they observed their states and witnessed them from when they were born until they grew up and claimed what they claimed of messengership. They did not see them engage in anything of that, nor did they practice it, nor did they accompany anyone who had knowledge and practice of it. The appearance of that at the hands of such people is a breaking of custom, so it would be a sufficient miracle. And God is the Grantor of success. And if they counter that with what appeared of the breaking of custom at the hand of Zarathustra, and that was not a proof of the truth of his claim, then similarly what you are claiming [is not a proof].
Source pages p. 707

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. The objector claims that supernatural acts could be achieved by anyone with sufficient effort, and that claimants have not tested everyone's abilities. The author answers that even if we concede the possibility, the prophets were known by their communities from birth; they never trained in such arts, nor associated with practitioners. Therefore, the appearance of such acts at their hands is truly a violation of custom and a valid miracle. The author then addresses a specific counter-example: Zarathustra who appeared to perform a custom-breaking act but was not a true prophet. The answer is that Zarathustra's act was not a genuine miracle (perhaps because it was not accompanied by a true claim or divine protection), so it does not disprove the rule.

تدرب

زرادشت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The miracle performed by Zarathustra proves that miracles are not unique to prophets.
Correction: Zarathustra's act was not a genuine miracle; it lacked divine confirmation and did not prove his claim, as implied by the author's dismissal.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the claim that prophets could have trained secretly to perform miracles?
A) He says that training is impossible for humans.
B) He points out that their communities witnessed their entire lives and saw no training.
C) He argues that God prevents all training.
D) He says that only magicians train.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are true signs of prophethood because prophets are publicly known to be untrained, and custom-breaking acts from false claimants do not qualify as genuine miracles.

Miracles Are Beyond Human Power
Al-Nasafi enumerates sensory miracles and asserts their exclusive divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles are events that lie beyond the scope of human capability and serve as divine confirmation of prophethood.

Core Idea
Miracles are not extraordinary human feats—they are exclusively from God.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi addresses a common misconception: that miracles are simply very impressive human acts. He lists concrete examples from Islamic tradition—the staff of Moses, the splitting of the sea, and others—and asserts that these are categorically beyond human power. The lesson clarifies why no rational person could think otherwise, and why this makes miracles a definitive proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the author's confident tone and the list of miracles.
2
Identify the miracles and their prophets
List the specific miracles mentioned. For each, recall which prophet performed it (Moses, Jesus, Muhammad). This connects the abstract claim to familiar stories.
The miracles are: staff to snake, splitting sea, reviving dead, splitting moon, water from fingers.
3
Understand the key assertion
Focus on the phrase 'ليست من أنواع ما يدخل تحت مقدور أحد غير الله تعالى' – these are not within anyone's power but God's. This is the central claim.
4
Reflect on the rational impossibility
Note the author's point that even the possibility of such acts from others 'does not occur to the heart of any rational person.' This strengthens the argument.
5
Connect to the conclusion
Since no one can produce similar miracles, opposition (i.e., challenging a prophet's claim) is impossible. Understand why this makes miracles a valid proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنه لا ريب لأحد لم يكن من شأنه العناد والمكابرة أن قلب العصا حية، وفلق البحر، وإحياء الموتى، وشق القمر، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع، وغير ذلك من هذه المعجزات الحسية، ليست من أنواع ما يدخل تحت مقدور أحد غير الله تعالى، وقد لا يخطر جواز ذلك من غير الله تعالى على قلب عاقل البتة، فلا يتمكن إذا فيه المعارضة.
Indeed, there is no doubt for anyone who is not characterized by stubbornness and obstinacy that the turning of the staff into a serpent, the splitting of the sea, the reviving of the dead, the cleaving of the moon, and the gushing of water from between the fingers, and other such sensory miracles, are not among the types of things that fall under the power of anyone other than God Almighty. And the possibility of that from other than God Almighty does not occur to the heart of any rational person at all. So opposition to it is not possible, therefore.
Source pages p. 707

Commentary
This passage asserts the miraculous nature of certain events and argues that they are beyond human capability. The author lists several well-known miracles from Islamic tradition (e.g., Moses' staff, splitting of the sea, Jesus reviving the dead, Muhammad's splitting of the moon, water from fingers). He states that no rational person would think such things could be done by anyone other than God. Therefore, no one can produce similar events to challenge a prophet's claim.

Misconception: Some think miracles are merely extraordinary human feats achievable through training or technology.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that miracles like turning a staff into a snake are not within the power of anyone other than God. They are categorically different from human abilities.

Checkpoint

B) They are beyond the power of anyone but God.
C) They are illusions.
D) They are not actually miracles.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine signs that lie beyond any human capacity, making them irrefutable proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you read or hear about the miracles of the prophets, do they produce awe and certainty in your heart, or have they become familiar stories that no longer shake you? What concrete step will you take today to renew your conviction that these events are divine proofs that demand your full submission?

Refutation of Miracles as Humanly Attainable
Refutes the objection that miracles can be acquired through effort.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a prophet's lack of training in miraculous acts proves that his miracles are genuinely divine and not a product of human effort.

Core Idea
A miracle is validated by the prophet's lack of practice, not by its impossibility to others.

The objection that miracles could be produced by human effort seems logical, but it misses a crucial point: prophets did not train for their miracles. This lesson walks through the refutation that even if miracles were learnable, the prophet's life history proves his miracle is a true violation of custom.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and refutation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the full argument. Notice the structure: an objection is presented, then refuted in two stages.
2
Analyze the conditional argument
Examine the first part of the refutation: even if we grant that miracles could be learned, the prophet's lack of effort makes his act a violation of custom, thus a proof.
The refutation uses a hypothetical agreement to strengthen its case.
3
Consider the community's testimony
Understand how the community's lifelong observation confirms that the prophet had no training or practice in the miraculous act, which solidifies that it is a divine miracle.
The community's knowledge is crucial evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة والرد عليها وبهذا كله يبطل قول من يقول: إن قلب العادة الذي أتى به مدعي الرسالة مما يمكن تحصيله لمن له في نوعه تكلف واجتهاد والمدعون ما امتحنوا قوى الجميع. على أنا نقول لهم: لو ساعدناكم لكان وجوده مما لم يكن له بذلك اجتهاد وتدرب واعتياد نقضا للمادة، فيكون دليلاً لصحة دعواهم، والمدعون للرسالة له لم يكن لهم بذلك اجتهاد ولا اعتياد عرف ذلك منهم قومهم الذين نشأوا هم بين أظهرهم، إذ عاينوا أحوالهم وشاهدوا منذ ولدوا إلى أن كبروا وادعوا ما ادعوا من الرسالة، فلم يروهم اشتغلوا بشيء من ذلك، ولا اعتادوا تعاطيه، ولا صحبوا من له بذلك علم واعتياد، وخروج ذلك على أيدي مثلهم ناقض للعادة، فكان معجزة كافية والله الموفق.
An objection and its refutation. And by all of this, the saying of those who say is invalidated: 'Indeed, the violation of custom that the claimant of prophethood brings about can be acquired by anyone who takes pains and strives in its type, and the claimants have not tested the powers of everyone.' However, we say to them: Even if we were to agree with you, its occurrence without any effort, training, or habit on his part would be a violation of the principle [that it requires effort], so it would be evidence for the truth of his claim. And the claimants of prophethood had no effort or habit in that, as their people who grew up among them knew, since they witnessed their conditions and saw them from the time they were born until they grew up and made their claims of prophethood. They did not see them occupied with anything of that, nor did they become accustomed to practicing it, nor did they accompany anyone who had knowledge and practice in it. And the appearance of that at the hands of such people is a violation of custom, so it is a sufficient miracle. And God grants success.
Source pages p. 707

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of an objection. The objection is that miracles (violations of custom) can be produced by humans through effort and training, and since not all human powers have been tested, one cannot be sure the prophet's miracle is unique. The refutation is: even if we grant that it is possible in principle, the specific prophets who brought miracles did not practice or train for them. Their communities observed them from childhood and never saw them engage in such practices. Therefore, their performing of these acts is still a violation of custom and thus constitutes a valid miracle.

Key Terms
قلب العادة
مدعي الرسالة
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are just advanced human skills that anyone with enough effort can achieve.
Correction: The prophet's lifelong lack of practice shows that his act cannot be attributed to effort, thus it is a divine miracle.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, why is the prophet's miracle still valid even if miracles could potentially be learned?
A) Because the prophet was more powerful.
B) Because the prophet did not train for it, unlike those who claim it can be learned.
C) Because the community was ignorant.
D) Because the miracle was witnessed by many.

Key Takeaway
The miracle's validity is established by the prophet's known lack of practice, not by the impossibility of human imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness a clear sign of Allah's guidance in your life, do you immediately try to explain it away as coincidence or your own effort, like the objectors in this passage? What would it mean for you to humbly accept it as a sign instead? Commit to one area where you will stop rationalizing and start acknowledging Allah's hand.
?
The prophet's community knew him intimately and saw no preparation for the miracle. Is there a person of piety in your life whose sudden spiritual growth you might dismiss because you think you know their past? Could that be a sign from Allah through them? Who is that person, and how will you respond differently now?
?
If you were to perform a miracle, would your community be surprised? The lesson shows that the prophet's lack of practice made his miracle valid. Are your good deeds the result of consistent training and habit, or are they occasional acts that would surprise those who know you? Are you relying on your own effort or on divine grace? Pledge to perform one act of worship this week that you have never done before, to rely on Allah's help alone.

Why Reliable Transmission Matters for Miracles
Refutes objection using Zoroaster by denying tawatur and affirming prophetic transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why isolated miracle reports are not reliable evidence for prophethood, while mass-transmitted prophetic miracles yield certain knowledge.

Core Idea
For a miracle to prove prophethood, its transmission must be beyond doubt.

In theological debates, skeptics sometimes point to miracle claims from false prophets. This passage from Imam al-Nasafi shows how to evaluate such claims: the key is not the miracle itself but how reliably it has been reported. We'll follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Realize that opponents compare prophetic miracles to Zoroaster's claimed miracles, arguing that if Zoroaster's miracles don't prove his claim, then prophetic miracles also don't prove theirs.
The objection is based on a false analogy.
2
Analyze the refutation
The author gives a two-part response: first, Zoroaster's reports lack tawatur (mass transmission) and are isolated, so they don't yield certain knowledge. Second, prophetic miracles are transmitted in a way that precludes falsehood.
Pay attention to the terms 'tawatur' and 'tawatu' (collusion).
3
Grasp the principle
Understand that the certainty of a miracle depends on the reliability of its transmission chain. This is a key principle in Islamic epistemology of prophethood.
This principle is used to defend the authenticity of prophetic miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قابلوا ذلك بما ظهر من الناقض للعادة على يدي زرادشت ولم يكن ذلك علمًا لصحة دعواه فكذا ما أنتم تدعونه. قلنا: لم يثبت شيء من ذلك بالتواتر بل المذكور أنه أدخل قوائم فرسه في بطنه في دار الملك بين يدي الملك وخواصه وكذا وضع طشت فيه نار على صدره فلم يضره ولم يكن عند ملأ من الناس. ومثل هذا الخبر لا يجب العلم بمخبره، لجواز التواطؤ على الكذب عليهم، بل الغالب من حال الملوك وأتباعهم، توليد أخبار لا صحة لها لما في ذلك من تمكين رعيتهم وتسوية أمور مملكتهم. فأما ما نقل من أعلام الرسل عليهم السلام فقد نقل على طريق لا احتمال فيه للكذب، ولا يتصور التواطؤ على النقلة، وما هذا سبيله من الأخبار فهو موجب للعلم الضروري على ما قررنا والله الموفق.
And if they counter that with what appeared of violation of custom at the hands of Zoroaster, and that did not constitute knowledge of the truth of his claim, then likewise what you claim [is invalid]. We said: Nothing of that has been established by tawātur (mass transmission). Rather, what is mentioned is that he inserted the legs of his horse into his belly in the king's palace before the king and his retinue, and likewise he placed a basin containing fire on his chest and it did not harm him, and this was not in the presence of a multitude of people. Such a report does not necessitate knowledge of its content, because of the possibility of collusion on lying. Rather, the common state of kings and their followers is that they generate baseless reports for the sake of controlling their subjects and managing their kingdom. As for what has been reported of the signs of the Messengers (peace be upon them), it has been reported in a manner that has no possibility of falsehood, and collusion on the part of the transmitters is inconceivable. Such reports necessitate necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī), as we have established. And God grants success.
Source pages p. 707

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection that Zoroaster also performed miracles but his claim was false. The response has two parts. First, the reports about Zoroaster are not reliably transmitted (not tawatur) and are isolated incidents witnessed only by a few, so they are not credible. Second, the reports about miracles of the prophets are transmitted in a way that precludes falsehood, giving necessary knowledge.

Key Terms
تواتر
علم ضروري
تواطؤ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any miracle claim, if reported, is equally credible.
Correction: This passage shows that the method of transmission (tawatur vs isolated) determines the level of certainty. Without mass transmission, collusion is possible, so the claim is not reliable.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author gives for rejecting the reported miracles of Zoroaster?
A) They are impossible.
B) They are not transmitted by tawatur.
C) They were performed by magic.
D) They were not witnessed by the prophet's followers.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic miracles are known through mass transmission (tawatur) which precludes collusion; isolated reports do not yield certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear claims about miracles or religious signs today—whether in a sermon, a video, or a book—do you examine how that information reached you? Are you as careful about the chain of transmission as this passage demands, or do you accept things on authority without verifying their tawatur?
?
The passage reveals that kings and their followers generate baseless reports to control people. Where in your own life—your political news, your community gossip, even your religious circles—are you uncritically absorbing narratives that might be fabricated for control? What would it mean for you to actively trace every significant claim you believe back to its source?
?
You now know that prophetic miracles are transmitted with a certainty that eliminates any possibility of falsehood. Does that certainty translate into a living conviction that changes how you respond to the Prophet's message (peace be upon him) today? Or is it merely an intellectual fact you store away without letting it move your heart to action?

Miracles support only possible claims, not impossible ones
Explains that a miracle cannot prove an inherently impossible claim like Zoroaster's.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a miracle can only authenticate a claim that is logically possible, and that an impossible claim like Zoroaster's cannot be proven by any miracle.

Core Idea
A miracle proves possibility, not impossibility.

We often assume a miracle proves any claim it accompanies. But Muslim theologians argue that a miracle only verifies what is possible, not what is inherently impossible. This passage explains why Zoroaster's claim to divinity fails, no matter what 'miracles' he might have performed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic carefully, then the English translation. Notice that the passage begins by stating the general ruling that a miracle indicates the possible, not the impossible.
The passage ends mid-sentence; focus on the complete argument.
2
Identify the key principle
The scholars state: 'The violation of custom indicates the realization of the possible, not the realization of that which is impossible.' This is the core principle.
Write this principle in your own words.
3
Understand why Zoroaster's claim is impossible
The passage details that Zoroaster's claim implies a creator who is ignorant, powerless, and generates a rival. Such a claim is 'impossible' (ممتنع) because it contradicts the necessary attributes of divinity.
List the defects mentioned: ignorance, powerlessness, subject to accidents.
4
Apply the principle to the example
Since Zoroaster's claim is impossible, no miracle can support it. The passage asks: 'Do you not see that the claim to divinity is not validated by such [supposed miracles] because of its impossibility?'
5
Reflect on the lesson's relevance
This principle protects the integrity of prophethood: miracles confirm true prophets because their claims are possible, but cannot validate false claims that are inherently contradictory.
Consider how this argument applies to other false claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب إلى هذا الجواب جميع متكلمي أهل الإسلام وأجاب بعض المحققين من علماء الأمة عن هذا فقال: إن الناقض للعادة يدل على ثبوت الممكن لا على ثبوت ما هو من الممتنع، ولهذا لا يكون دليلاً على صحة دعوى التأله، ودعوى زرادشت دعوى ممتنعة لما فيها من القول بصانع عاجز جاهل، تولد من فكرته الردية من يعاديه ويزاحمه في ملكه وينازعه في سلطانه وهو غير عالم بعاقبة فكره، عاجز عن قهر عدوه وغلبته، وهو مع هذا محل للحوادث، إذ حدثت فيه فكرته الرديئة، وكل ذلك دعوى ممتنعة ظاهر عوارها بإفسادها، ومثل هذا لا بالدليل - ألا يرى أن دعوى المتأله لا تصح بمثل هذا لما فيها من الامتناع. يحققه أن قيام المعجزة على يدي المتنبئ إنما لا يجوز لئلا يؤدي إلى
All the theologians (mutakallimūn) of Islam adopted this answer, and some verifying scholars of the community answered this [objection] saying: Indeed, the violation of custom indicates the realization of the possible, not the realization of that which is impossible. Therefore, it cannot be evidence for the truth of a claim to divinity. And the claim of Zoroaster is an impossible claim, because it involves asserting a creator who is powerless and ignorant, from whose evil thought emanated someone who opposes him, vies with him in his kingdom, and contends with him in his authority, while he is unaware of the outcome of his thought, powerless to overcome his enemy and defeat him. Moreover, he is subject to accidents, since his evil thought occurred within him. All of that is an impossible claim whose defect is apparent in its corruption. Such a thing cannot be proven by evidence. Do you not see that the claim to divinity is not validated by such [supposed miracles] because of its impossibility. He confirms that the occurrence of a miracle at the hands of a false prophet is not allowed, lest it lead to
Source pages p. 708

Commentary
This passage presents a second, more profound answer from some scholars. The argument is that a miracle (violation of custom) only proves the possibility of the claim it supports, not its impossibility. Zoroaster's claim is inherently impossible because it implies a defective creator (a god who is powerless, ignorant, and generates a rival). Since the claim is impossible, no miracle can support it. The passage begins by noting that this answer was adopted by all Muslim theologians, and then gives the answer of the verifying scholars.

Key Terms
ممتنع
ممكن
دعوى التأله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any miracle proves the truth of the claim it accompanies.
Correction: A miracle only indicates the possibility of the claim; an impossible claim cannot be proven by any miracle, no matter how extraordinary.

Checkpoint
According to the verifying scholars, why cannot Zoroaster's supposed miracles prove his claim?
A) Because the miracles were not witnessed by many.
B) Because his claim is logically impossible.
C) Because miracles cannot prove any claim.
D) Because Zoroaster was not a prophet.

Key Takeaway
A miracle affirms only what is rationally possible; it cannot validate an inherently contradictory claim like Zoroaster's.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been drawn to a religious claim because of a dramatic story or miracle, without first examining whether the claim itself is logically possible? What would it mean for your faith if you prioritized reason over spectacle?
?
The passage shows that even a supernatural event cannot validate a distorted image of God. Are there any hidden assumptions about God's power or knowledge in your heart that might actually contradict His perfection? Will you take time this week to compare those thoughts with the Quran's description of Allah?
?
Zoroaster's claim made God weak and ignorant—do you ever act as if God is limited by your circumstances, or doubt that He knows the outcome of your struggles? How can you replace those subtle impossibilities with firm trust in His complete power and wisdom?

Miracles
beginner
5 min
The Mutawatir Transmission of Prophetic Miracles
Nasafi contrasts unreliable stories with mutawatir prophetic miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why reports of prophetic miracles are considered epistemically certain (necessary knowledge) while other miracle stories are not.

Core Idea
Prophetic miracles are transmitted in a way that makes falsehood impossible.

Imam Nasafi addresses a common objection: how can we be sure that the miracles attributed to prophets really happened? He begins by dismissing a story about a king's horse and a fire pan, noting that it was not witnessed by enough people and could be fabricated. He then contrasts this with the reports of the signs of the messengers, which are transmitted in such a way that collusion and falsehood are inconceivable. This distinction is crucial for establishing the reliability of prophetic miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: first a rejection of a weak report, then the positive argument for prophetic miracles.
Focus on the contrast between the two types of reports.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the two types of reports discussed: the non-mutawatir king story and the mutawatir prophetic signs. Note how Nasafi distinguishes them.
3
Understand 'necessary knowledge'
The passage concludes that prophetic miracles produce necessary knowledge. Reflect on what that means: knowledge that is immediate and certain, not based on inference.
This is a key concept in Islamic epistemology.
4
Connect to wider theology
Ask: Why is it important that prophetic miracles are certain? Because they provide a basis for believing in prophecy itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا: لم يثبت شيء من ذلك بالتواتر بل المذكور أنه أدخل قوائم فرسه في بطنه في دار الملك بين يدي الملك وخواصه وكذا وضع طشت فيه نار على صدره فلم يضره ولم يكن عند ملأ من الناس. ومثل هذا الخبر لا يجب العلم بمخبره، لجواز التواطؤ على الكذب عليهم، بل الغالب من حال الملوك وأتباعهم، توليد أخبار لا صحة لها لما في ذلك من تمكين رعيتهم وتسوية أمور مملكتهم. فأما ما نقل من أعلام الرسل عليهم السلام فقد نقل على طريق لا احتمال فيه للكذب، ولا يتصور التواطؤ على النقلة، وما هذا سبيله من الأخبار فهو موجب للعلم الضروري على ما قررنا والله الموفق.
We say: Nothing of that has been established by mutawatir (mass transmission), but what is mentioned is that he inserted the legs of his horse into its belly in the king's palace before the king and his retinue, and likewise he placed a tray containing fire on his chest and it did not harm him, and this was not in the presence of a multitude of people. Such a report does not necessitate knowledge of its content, because of the possibility of collusion in lying against them. Rather, the usual state of kings and their followers is to generate reports that have no truth, because of what is in that of solidifying their subjects and settling matters of their kingdom. As for what is transmitted from the signs of the messengers (peace be upon them), it has been transmitted in a way that has no possibility of falsehood, and collusion among the transmitters is inconceivable. Such reports necessitate necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī) according to what we have established. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 708

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the reliability of reports of miracles. The author begins by rejecting a specific story about a king's horse and a fire pan, saying it is not mutawatir and could be fabricated. He then contrasts this with the reports of the signs (miracles) of the messengers, which are transmitted in a way that precludes falsehood and collusion. These reports, he says, produce necessary knowledge (ʿilm ḍarūrī). The passage thus establishes the epistemological basis for accepting prophetic miracles.

Key Terms
تواتر
علم ضروري
أعلام الرسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All miracle stories are equally reliable and should be accepted as evidence.
Correction: Nasafi shows that only mutawatir reports (where collusion is impossible) yield certain knowledge; non-mutawatir stories can be fabricated.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that reports of prophetic miracles compel necessary knowledge?
A) They are witnessed by many people.
B) They are transmitted in a way that precludes falsehood and collusion.
C) They are recorded in sacred books.
D) They are confirmed by kings.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic miracles are transmitted mutawatir, producing necessary knowledge that is certain and beyond doubt.

?

The passage distinguishes between reports that can be fabricated and those that cannot. In your own life, where do you get your certainty about religious matters? Is it based on reliable transmission or on weak reports? What steps can you take to strengthen your reliance on mutawatir knowledge?

Nasafi says the usual state of kings is to generate false reports. Where in your life do you accept stories from authorities without checking? How can you apply this lesson's criteria to evaluate claims you hear today, especially about religion?

Miracles Only Affirm Possible Claims
Scholars argue miracles confirm only possible claims, rejecting Zoroaster's impossible divinity claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a miracle can only confirm a claim that is rationally possible, not one that is inherently impossible.

Core Idea
A miracle is evidence for the possible, not the impossible.

Theologians offered a refined response to the objection that false prophets or claimants to divinity might also perform miracles. They argued that a miracle, as a violation of custom, only establishes the truth of a claim that is possible in itself. An impossible claim—like Zoroaster's ascribing weakness to God—cannot be supported by any miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the key principle
The passage states that the violation of custom (miracle) indicates the existence of the possible, not the impossible. Read this carefully.
This is the central thesis of the lesson.
2
Understand the example of Zoroaster
The scholars explain why Zoroaster's claim of divinity is impossible: it implies a weak, ignorant Creator subject to accidents. Recognise the impossibility.
The impossibility makes the claim ineligible for proof by miracle.
3
Grasp the verification argument
If the claim were possible, a miracle on a false prophet would cause confusion or imply God's weakness. But with an impossible claim, no such problem arises.
This reasoning shows why miracles can still occur for impossible claims, but they don't prove them.
4
Apply the distinction
Distinguish between a possible claim (like prophethood) that can be confirmed by a miracle, and an impossible claim (like divinity of a creature) that cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب إلى هذا الجواب جميع متكلمي أهل الإسلام وأجاب بعض المحققين من علماء الأمة عن هذا فقال: إن الناقض للعادة يدل على ثبوت الممكن لا على ثبوت ما هو من الممتنع، ولهذا لا يكون دليلاً على صحة دعوى التأله، ودعوى زرادشت دعوى ممتنعة لما فيها من القول بصانع عاجز جاهل، تولد من فكرته الردية من يعاديه ويزاحمه في ملكه وينازعه في سلطانه وهو غير عالم بعاقبة فكره، عاجز عن قهر عدوه وغلبته، وهو مع هذا محل للحوادث، إذ حدثت فيه فكرته الرديئة، وكل ذلك دعوى ممتنعة ظاهر عوارها بإفسادها، ومثل هذا لا يصح بالدليل - ألا يرى أن دعوى المتأله لا تصح بمثل هذا لما فيها من الامتناع. يحققه أن قيام المعجزة على يدي المتنبئ إنما لا يجوز لئلا يؤدي إلى التسوية بين الحق والباطل أو إلى تعجيز الباري عن إقامة الدليل على ما من الدعاوي والتفرقة بين الحق منها والباطل، وإنما تثبت التسوية أو العجز عن التفرقة إذا كانت الدعوى في نفسها ممكنة غير ممتنعة، فأما عند امتناعها فلا يؤدي إلى ذلك، ولهذا كان قيام الناقض للعادة على يدي المتأله ممكنا غير ممتنع، والله الموفق.
All the theologians (mutakallimūn) of the people of Islam went to this answer. And some of the verifying scholars of the community answered about this, saying: The violator of custom (al-nāqiḍ li-l-ʿādah) indicates the existence of the possible, not the existence of what is impossible (al-mumtaniʿ). For this reason, it is not evidence for the validity of the claim of divinity. The claim of Zoroaster is an impossible claim because it contains the statement of a Creator who is weak and ignorant, from whose evil thought is generated one who opposes him, vies with him in his dominion, contests him in his authority, while he is unaware of the outcome of his thought, incapable of repressing his enemy and overcoming him. And with all this, he is a locus of accidents, since his evil thought occurred in him. All of this is an impossible claim, its defect is apparent due to its corruption. Such a thing is not established by evidence – do you not see that the claim of one claiming divinity is not valid by such a thing because of the impossibility in it? He verifies this: The occurrence of a miracle at the hands of a false claimant to prophethood (al-mutanabbī) is not permitted, lest it lead to equating truth and falsehood or to incapacitating the Creator from establishing evidence for whatever claims there are and distinguishing truth from falsehood. Equating or inability to distinguish only become established when the claim itself is possible and not impossible. But when it is impossible, it does not lead to that. For this reason, the occurrence of the violator of custom at the hands of one claiming divinity (al-mutaʾallih) is possible and not impossible. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 708

Commentary
This passage presents a second answer from some verifying scholars. They argue that a miracle (nāqiḍ al-ʿādah) only indicates the existence of something possible, not something impossible. Therefore, Zoroaster's claim of divinity is impossible because it implies a weak, ignorant creator, etc. Such a claim cannot be proven by a miracle. Then they verify this by stating that a miracle cannot occur on a false prophet if the claim is possible, because it would cause confusion or incapacitate God. But if the claim is impossible, no confusion arises, so the miracle could occur. Hence, Zoroaster's miracles, if any, do not prove his divinity because his claim is impossible.

Key Terms
ناقض العادة
ممتنع
ممكن
متنبئ
متأله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If someone performs a miracle, it automatically proves that his claim is true, regardless of what he claims.
Correction: A miracle only confirms a claim that is rationally possible. An impossible claim, like ascribing divinity to a creature with weaknesses, cannot be proven by any miracle.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Zoroaster's claim of divinity not become proven even if miracles occurred?
A) Because his miracles were not genuine violations of custom.
B) Because his claim is impossible, and miracles only confirm possible claims.
C) Because he was not a prophet.
D) Because his followers fabricated the miracles.

Key Takeaway
A miracle can only serve as evidence for a claim that is rationally possible; an impossible claim remains unproven regardless of miraculous events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever let an impressive miracle or sign convince you of a belief without first checking whether that belief is even logically possible? What belief in your life needs to be examined for its rational consistency?
?
If a miracle can only confirm what is possible, then the most important evidence for the truth of Islam is not extraordinary events but the soundness of its core claims about God. Are you actively seeking to understand and verify those claims, or are you relying on emotional experiences? What is one step you will take this week to study the intellectual proofs for tawheed?
?
The passage calls you to distinguish between possible and impossible claims about God. Are there any aspects of your understanding of God that might be logically inconsistent? Would you be willing to revise them even if they feel familiar or comforting?

The Condition for Miracles as Proofs
Defines the condition for miracles to distinguish truth from falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational condition that must be met for a miracle to serve as a proof distinguishing true claims from false ones.

Core Idea
A miracle only proves a possible claim, not an impossible one.

This brief passage from Imam al-Nasafi establishes a crucial principle in kalam: miracles are not magical proofs for any claim. They only authenticate claims that are themselves rationally possible. This prevents the misuse of miracles to support contradictory or absurd propositions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms like mumkin (possible) and mumtaniʿ (impossible).
The passage is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the condition
Find the sentence that states when the equalization or incapacitation is established. It hinges on the claim being possible, not impossible.
3
Consider the example
The author gives the example of a miracle (nāqiḍ al-ʿāda) occurring at the hands of a godly person. Why is this possible? Reflect on the connection.
The example illustrates the principle.
4
Apply the principle
Think of an impossible claim, like '2+2=5'. Could a miracle prove it? According to this passage, no.
This guards against a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التسوية بين (۱) الحق والباطل أو إلى تعجيز الباري عن إقامة الدليل على ما من الدعاوي والتفرقة بين الحق منها والباطل، وإنما تثبت التسوية أو العجز عن التفرقة إذا كانت الدعوى في نفسها ممكنة غير ممتنعة، فأما عند امتناعها (۲) فلا يؤدي إلى ذلك، ولهذا كان قيام الناقض للعادة على يدي المتأله ممكنا غير ممتنع، والله الموفق.
The equalization between truth and falsehood or the incapacitation of the Creator from establishing proof for some of the claims and distinguishing between the truth and falsehood of them is only established when the claim is in itself possible, not impossible. But when it is impossible, it does not lead to that. For this reason, the occurrence of a miracle (nāqiḍ al-ʿāda) at the hands of a godly person is possible, not impossible. God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 709

Commentary
This passage defines the epistemological condition under which miracles (nawāqiḍ al-ʿāda) can serve as proofs distinguishing true claims from false ones. It states that if a claim is inherently possible, then a miracle can authenticate it; but if the claim is impossible (e.g., claiming something logically contradictory), then a miracle does not prove it. The author emphasizes that miracles themselves are possible and therefore can testify for possible claims. This principle is fundamental in kalam for evaluating prophetic claims.

Misconception: Some think that any miracle proves any claim, even impossible ones.
Correction: This passage clarifies that miracles only support possible claims; an impossible claim cannot be proven by a miracle.

B) When the claim is possible
C) When the miracle is performed by any person
D) When the miracle is witnessed by many

Key Takeaway
A miracle can only serve as proof for a claim that is rationally possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Prophet's Miracles Surpass Natural and Psychic Powers
Al-Nasafi classifies miracles as beyond natural and psychic powers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the miracles of a true prophet are categorically beyond the capabilities of natural forces and psychic tricks, affirming his divine claim.

Core Idea
Miracles are not tricks; they are divine acts beyond all natural and psychic limits.

Al-Nasafi now presents the second argument for prophethood: the prophet's miracle matches his divine claim. He explains that such wonders cannot be produced by natural laws or psychic arts. This lesson unpacks why miracles are uniquely divine evidences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of Al-Nasafi's argument.
Notice the detailed examples used to illustrate the point.
2
Identify the two dismissed categories
Al-Nasafi excludes two sources of extraordinary acts. Find them and note how he describes each.
The categories are natural forces and psychic forces.
3
Reflect on the examples
Consider the specific miracles listed (reviving sheep, speaking camel, etc.). Why does Al-Nasafi think they are impossible under nature or psychic powers?
This reflection helps internalize the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما بينته فمطابقة لدعواه أنه ادعى أمرًا إلهيًا وأتى بالبينات الإلهية التي تفوق قوى الخلق، ولن يأتى حصولها بالقوى الطبيعية - فإن المحققين في معرفة الأصول الطبيعية العارفين بما يجوز أن يترتب تحتها وما لا يجوز متيقنون أن إحياء الشاة المصلية وإنطاق الناقة وإلجاء الأسطوانة إلى الحنين، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع، مما لا يجوز ترتبها تحت أسرار الطبائع ، وكذا شق القمر وغيره على ما نبين إذا انتهينا إلى إقامة الدليل على ذلك إن شاء الله تعالى - ولا بالقوى النفسانية إذ الملتحق بالتدابير النفسانية إما أن يترتب تحت السحر والعزائم أو تحت اللطف والشعبذة، والعالمون بهذه الأمور يعرفون أن ما أتى به من المعجزات خارج عن هذه الوجوه، ونكشف عن ذلك أيضا بعد هذا إن شاء الله تعالى.
As for his proof, it matches his claim: he claimed a divine matter and brought divine evidences that surpass the powers of creation. They cannot be obtained by natural forces—for the investigators knowledgeable in natural principles, who know what may and may not fall under them, are certain that reviving the grilled sheep, making the she-camel speak, compelling the pillar to yearn, and water springing from between the fingers cannot fall under the secrets of natures, likewise the splitting of the moon and other things as we will explain when we come to establish the proof for that, God willing—nor by psychic forces, for what is attached to psychic devices either falls under sorcery and incantations or under subtlety and sleight of hand. Those knowledgeable in these matters know that the miracles he brought are outside these categories, and we will also uncover that after this, God willing.
Source pages p. 714

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument: the prophet's proof (miracle) matches his divine claim. It classifies miracles as beyond two categories: natural forces and psychic forces. Natural forces cannot produce such wonders as reviving a roasted sheep, causing a she-camel to speak, making a pillar long for the prophet, water flowing from fingers, or splitting the moon. Psychic forces are either sorcery, incantations, or sleight of hand, and the prophet's miracles are outside these. Thus, his proof is uniquely divine.

الأصول الطبيعية
القوى النفسانية
السحر
العزائم
اللطف
الشعبذة

Misconception: Miracles are just extremely rare natural events or clever tricks.
Correction: Al-Nasafi insists that miracles are categorically beyond nature and psychic tricks, making them uniquely divine.

A) Divine and satanic
B) Natural forces and psychic forces
C) Sorcery and miracles
D) Reason and revelation

Key Takeaway
The prophet's miracles are divine proofs because they surpass the capacities of both nature and human psychic arts.
