Miracles Transcend Natural and Psychic Causes
Author rejects natural and psychic explanations for miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic theologians argue that miracles cannot be explained by natural laws or psychic powers.

Core Idea
Miracles break the rules of nature and magic alike.

The author begins by establishing that miracles are not simply extraordinary natural events or psychic tricks. He appeals to the knowledge of natural principles and psychic arts to show that the miracles of prophets fall outside both categories. This sets the stage for his positive proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's argument sink in before analyzing it.
Notice the repetition at the end, which may be a copy error.
2
Identify the two rejected explanations
The passage rejects two possible sources for miracles: natural laws (asrar al-taba'i') and psychic powers (al-quwa al-nafsaniyya). Find where each is mentioned.
The author argues that both are inadequate.
3
List the miracle examples
Write down the four miracles mentioned: reviving a roasted sheep, making a camel speak, causing a pillar to yearn, and making water flow from fingers. Also note the splitting of the moon.
These are well-known miracles in Islamic tradition.
4
Understand the contrast with sorcery
The author says psychic powers fall under sorcery, spells, or sleight of hand. Miracles are not like these because they are beyond human capacity and are signs from God.
This distinction protects prophethood from accusations of magic.
5
Note the promise of future proof
The author says he will explain the proof for miracles later. This lesson is just the negative argument; the positive proof comes next.
This creates anticipation and shows the structure of the larger work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصول الطبيعية العارفين بما يجوز أن يترتب تحتها وما لا يجوز متيقنون أن إحياء الشاة المصليَّة وإنطاق الناقة وإلجاء الأسطوانة إلى الحنين، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع، مما لا يجوز ترتبها تحت أسرار الطبائع ، وكذا شق القمر وغيره على ما نبين إذا انتهينا إلى إقامة الدليل على ذلك إن شاء الله تعالى - ولا بالقوى النفسانية إذ الملتحق بالتدابير النفسانية إما أن يترتب تحت السحر والعزائم أو تحت اللطف والشعبذة، والعالمون بهذه الأمور يعرفون أن ما أتى به من المعجزات خارج عن هذه الوجوه، ونكشف عن ذلك أيضا بعد هذا ذلك أيضًا بعد هذا - إن شاء الله تعالى.
Those who know the natural principles, what may and may not be subsumed under them, are certain that reviving a roasted sheep, causing a she-camel to speak, compelling a pillar to yearn, and causing water to flow from between fingers are things that cannot be subsumed under the secrets of natures, and likewise the splitting of the moon and other [miracles] as we will explain when we come to establishing the proof of that, God willing. And [they are] also not [due to] psychic powers, for what is attached to psychic devices is either subsumed under sorcery and spells or under prestidigitation and sleight of hand, and those knowledgeable of these matters know that what he brought of miracles is outside these categories, and we will uncover that also after this, that also after this—God willing.
Source pages p. 715

Commentary
This passage argues that miracles (mu‘jizat) are not caused by natural laws or psychic powers. The author first appeals to those who understand natural principles (al-usul al-tabi‘iyya) and are certain that certain events—like reviving a cooked sheep, speaking of a camel, a pillar yearning, water flowing from fingers, the splitting of the moon—cannot be explained by natural causality. Then he argues they are also not from psychic powers (al-quwa al-nafsaniyya), because psychic phenomena fall under sorcery, spells, or illusion, while miracles transcend these. The author promises further proof later.

Key Terms
أسرار الطبائع
القوى النفسانية
المعجزات
السحر
الشعبذة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are merely unusual events that could eventually be explained by science or advanced magic.
Correction: The author argues that those who truly understand natural principles and psychic arts know that miracles cannot be subsumed under either category. They are categorically different.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are miracles not attributable to natural causes?
A) Because natural causes are unknown
B) Because those knowledgeable in natural principles know such events cannot occur under them
C) Because miracles are always performed by sorcerers
D) Because natural causes only apply to inanimate objects

Key Takeaway
Miracles are categorically different from natural events and psychic tricks, serving as divine signs of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever witnessed or experienced something that you knew was beyond nature or human ability, yet you explained it away as coincidence or psychology? What did that decision reveal about your heart's posture towards the divine? Will you commit to recognizing such signs as Allah's direct intervention from now on?
?

When will you next test your reliance on Him in a situation that seems impossible?
?
When the author insists that miracles are 'outside these categories,' he is forcing you to choose: will you submit to the supernatural Lordship of Allah, or will you reduce His signs to something you can explain? Which category have you been placing Allah's favors in, and how will you repent from that intellectual arrogance today?

4 min
Three Categories of Sensory Signs and External Miracles
Classification of sensory signs into three categories with examples of external miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's classification of sensory signs into three categories and be able to identify examples of external miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles are classified into three types: external to the Prophet, within him, and in his character.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a foundational classification of sensory signs (adilla hissiyya) that confirm prophethood. The author divides them into three categories based on their relationship to the Prophet’s essence and character. We will examine the first category—external miracles—through a list of well-known events witnessed by many companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Identify the three categories of sensory signs that the author enumerates. Note the phrases 'خارج ذاته', 'في ذاته', and 'في أخلاقه'.
These are the three divisions: external, personal, and character-based.
2
Explore the external miracles
Go through the list of miracles external to the Prophet's essence. Reflect on how each miracle serves as a sensory sign confirming prophethood.
Examples include the splitting of the moon and the moaning of the wood.
3
Reflect on the misconception
Many assume that all miracles are external. Consider that the author also includes internal and character-based signs, expanding our understanding of prophetic evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي أقسام ثلاثة: فمنها ما كان خارج ذاته، ومنها ما كان في ذاته ومنها ما كان في أخلاقه. فأما ما كان خارج ذاته فمن نحو انشقاق القمر، واجتذاب الشجرة، وتسليم الحجر عليه، وشرب الكثير من الشرب القليل من الماء، ونبع الماء من بين أصابعه، وحنين الخشب، وشكاية الناقة وشهادة الشاة المصلية، وما كان من السحاب الذي كان يظله قبل مبعثه، وما كان من حال أبي جهل عليه اللعنة وصخرته حين هوى بها إلى رأسه، وما كان من شأن الشاه الحابل ودرها حين مسح بيده الكريمة على ضرعها على ما ذكر في حديث أم معبد.
And they are three divisions: some of them were external to his essence, some were in his essence, and some were in his character. As for what was external to his essence: examples are the splitting of the moon, the drawing of the tree, the greeting of the stone, the drinking of many from a small drink of water, the gushing of water from between his fingers, the moaning of the wood, the complaint of the she-camel, the testimony of the roasted sheep, the cloud that used to give him shade before his mission, the incident of Abu Jahl (may curse be upon him) and his rock when it fell upon his head, and the affair of the sheep of al-Habil and its milk when he wiped his noble hand on its udder as mentioned in the hadith of Umm Ma'bad.
Source pages p. 719

Commentary
This passage presents the author's classification of sensory signs into three categories: (1) those external to the Prophet's essence (khārij dhātihi), (2) those in his essence (fī dhātihi), and (3) those in his character (fī akhlāqihi). The author then elaborates on the first category by providing a list of well-known miracles: the splitting of the moon, the tree coming to him, stones greeting him, water multiplying, water flowing from his fingers, the wooden pole moaning, the she-camel complaining, the roasted sheep speaking, the cloud shading him before prophethood, the story of Abu Jahl's rock, and the miracle of the sheep giving milk when he wiped its udder, as recorded in the hadith of Umm Ma'bad. These examples illustrate the external sensory signs that were witnessed by many and confirm his prophethood.

Key Terms
خارج ذاته
في ذاته
في أخلاقه
انشقاق القمر
حنين الخشب
شهادة الشاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All miracles are external and visible to others.
Correction: The author includes miracles that are personal (in his essence) and character-based, showing that prophethood is confirmed by inner and outer signs.

Checkpoint
How many categories of sensory signs does the author list?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Sensory proofs of prophethood are not limited to external wonders; they also include the Prophet’s personal qualities and character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about external miracles like the splitting of the moon and the tree drawing near. Do you truly believe these events happened exactly as described, or do you subconsciously treat them as distant stories? If you honestly doubted one of them, how would that affect your trust in the Prophet's message?
?
The Prophet's external miracles were witnessed by many people, yet some still rejected him. Today, you have these reports transmitted to you. What is preventing you from having the same certainty as those who saw them? Is it lack of imagination, or is there a deeper hesitation in your heart?
?
Among the miracles listed is the sheep that testified. Imagine that event: a cooked sheep speaking. Does your heart feel awe at this miracle, or has it become just another fact? What would it take for you to feel the same wonder as a companion who witnessed it? What can you do this week to revive that sense of amazement in your faith?

5 min
Miraculous Signs in the Prophet's Essence
The author enumerates miraculous signs in the Prophet's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sensory miracles associated with the Prophet's physical nature as proofs of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's very being was filled with miraculous signs.

This lesson presents the second category of sensory proofs: those in the Prophet's essence (fī dhātihi). Unlike external miracles, these signs are part of his own person — the light that passed through his lineage, the seal of prophethood, his surpassing beauty, fragrance, and even his sweat being beneficial. These are not just historical details; they are evidences that his role as a prophet was manifest in his very being.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on miraculous signs
Read the Arabic and translation for the first part of the source, focusing on the list of signs in the Prophet's essence.
Notice the use of 'fī dhātihi' (in his essence) as the organizing category.
2
Identify each miraculous sign
List each sign: the light, the seal, his height surpassing tall men, his beauty compared to the moon, his fragrance, and the benefit of his sweat.
These are all sensory, observable signs.
3
Consider why these are proofs
Ask: how does each sign point to prophethood? For example, the light signifies divine selection, the seal is a physical stamp of prophethood, and his beauty indicates perfection of creation.
These are not ordinary human traits; they are extraordinary.
4
Reflect on the category
Contrast these 'internal' sensory signs with external miracles (like splitting the moon). Why would the author include them as proofs?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما كان في ذاته فنحو النور الذي كان ينتقل من ظهر إلى بطن إلى ظهر إلى أن خرج، وما كان من الخاتم بين كتفيه، وما وصف أنه كان ربعة ثم كان لا يزاحم طويلين إلا فاقهما، وما روى أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن، وأنه كان أطيب ريحا من المسك وألين من الحرير، وكان يؤخذ عرقه فينتفع به في الطيب، وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنا وجمالا، وروي في وصفه على التفصيل أنه عليه السلام كان أطول من المربوع، وأقصر من المشذب، عظيم الهامة، رجل الشعر، أزهر اللون، واسع الجبين، أزج الحواجب، أقنى العرنين، يحسبه من لم يتأمله أشم، في عينيه دبح، وفي سطع، وفي لحيته كثافة، سهل الخدين، ضليع الفم، مفلج الأسنان، ظاهر الوضاءة، عظيم الصدر، سواء البطن، ضخم الكراديس، بعيد ما بين المنكبين، دقيق المسبوبة، طويل الزندين، رحب الراحة، شثن الكفين، سائل الأطراف، بادن متماسك، وسيم، قسيم، فخم، مفخم، ليس بالجافي ولا المهين، وصفت بهذا هند بن أبي هالة بين يدي المهاجرين والأنصار بهذه الحلية - وكان وصافا - فصدق بها. وكذا وصفته أم معبد لزوجها بما يضاهي هذا فلم ينكر عليها.
And as for what was in his essence: examples are the light that transferred from back to belly to back until it emerged, and the seal between his shoulders, and what was described that he was of medium stature, then he would not contend with tall men except that he surpassed them, and what was narrated that he looked at his face and at the full moon, and he was more beautiful, and that he was more fragrant than musk and softer than silk, and his sweat was taken and benefited from in perfume, and his creation was described in a way that no one is known to be described with such beauty and comeliness, and it is narrated in his detailed description that he, peace be upon him, was taller than the medium-height but shorter than the lanky, large-headed, with flowing hair, bright white with a reddish tint, wide forehead, arched eyebrows, a prominent bridge of the nose, one who did not examine him might think he was aquiline-nosed, with slight redness in the eyes, a narrow line of hair on the chest, thick beard, smooth cheeks, wide mouth, spaced teeth, apparent brightness, large chest, flat belly, large joints, wide between the shoulders, delicate collarbones, long forearms, spacious palms, thick-fingered hands yet soft, tapered limbs, solid yet compact, handsome, of good countenance, majestic, dignified, neither rough nor despicable. Hind ibn Abi Hala described him with this before the Muhajirun and Ansar—and he was a good describer—and they confirmed it. Likewise, Umm Ma'bad described him to her husband with something similar, and he did not deny it.
Source pages p. 719

Commentary
This passage details the second category of sensory signs: those in the Prophet's essence (fī dhātihi). The author begins by listing miraculous aspects of his physical nature: the light that passed through his lineage from father to mother until his birth, the seal of prophethood between his shoulders, his surpassing beauty compared to the full moon, his fragrance better than musk, his softness, and the beneficial use of his sweat. Then he provides a detailed physical description of the Prophet, citing the description by Hind ibn Abi Hala (the son of Khadija from a previous marriage) which was publicly recited in the presence of the companions and confirmed. This description includes height, hair color, complexion, forehead, eyebrows, nose, eyes, chest, hands, and overall form. Finally, he mentions that Umm Ma'bad gave a similar description to her husband, which was accepted. This detailed description serves as a sensory proof of his prophethood, as it records an extraordinary beauty and perfection that could not be fabricated.

Key Terms
في ذاته
نور
خاتم النبوة
ربعة
بدر
مسك
عرق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These miraculous signs are just myths or exaggerations, not historical facts.
Correction: These signs are documented in multiple authentic narrations and were accepted by the Companions as real sensory evidence of prophethood.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is mentioned as a sensory sign in the Prophet's essence?
A) His height being exactly average
B) The seal between his shoulders
C) His long beard
D) His strong voice

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's physical being itself contained sensory miracles that serve as proofs of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's sweat was collected and used as perfume. Do you treat even the smallest remnants of his sunnah as precious blessings? What sunnah will you intentionally revive this week, not as a ritual, but as a way to draw closer to his blessed example?
?
His beauty surpassed the full moon. When you gaze at the moon, does your heart ache to see his face in the hereafter? What concrete step will you take today to increase your love for him so that this longing becomes your driving force?
?
The light passed through pure lineages from prophet to prophet until it reached him. Are you aware of the spiritual lineage you are building for your children or those around you? What sin or negligence are you tolerating that might dim the light of faith in your household?

The Prophet's Detailed Physical Description
The author provides a detailed physical description from two narrators as a sensory proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed physical description of the Prophet as narrated by his companions and its significance as a sensory proof.

Core Idea
The Prophet's physical description was preserved as a witness to his perfect creation.

After mentioning miraculous signs, the author provides a detailed physical description of the Prophet, citing two narrations: one from Hind ibn Abi Hala, who described him before the Muhajirun and Ansar, and a similar one from Umm Ma'bad. This description includes every aspect of his appearance—from his height to his hands—and was publicly confirmed. Such detailed preservation of an individual's physical traits serves as a testament to his extraordinary nature and prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the detailed description
Read the Arabic and translation for the second part of the source, focusing on the physical traits listed.
Try to visualize the description as you read.
2
Note the narrators
Identify that this description comes from Hind ibn Abi Hala (recited publicly) and Umm Ma'bad (to her husband). Both were accepted without denial.
Multiple witnesses strengthen the reliability.
3
Understand the purpose
Consider why such a detailed description is included as a proof of prophethood. It shows the Prophet's perfection and that his appearance was extraordinary.
It is not merely biographical but evidentiary.

Miracles and the Proof from Tawatur of Ahad Reports
Nasafi discusses how ahad reports of miracles can be collectively probative through tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how reports transmitted through single chains (ahad) can collectively provide certain proof of prophethood through the principle of tawatur (multiple independent transmissions).

Core Idea
Multiple independent transmission of miracle reports yields certainty even if each chain alone is weak.

Nasafi acknowledges the overwhelming number of the Prophet's miracles but notes that some are transmitted via ahad chains. He then addresses a key methodological question: How can such reports serve as proof? In this passage, he explains the role of tawatur in transforming ahad reports into evidence for the general occurrence of miracles, using an analogy from famous historical figures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and its English translation. Notice the author's flow: abundance of miracles, then a methodological turn, then the condition for ahad reports to be probative.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main argument is complete.
2
Identify the problem
Nasafi states that ahad reports do not individually give certain knowledge. Find that statement and understand its implication: without additional conditions, such reports are insufficient.
This is a key methodological point.
3
Identify the solution: tawatur
Locate the condition 'unless they are transmitted by people for whom collusion on lying is inconceivable.' This is the concept of tawatur. Understand how multiple independent lines create certainty.
The Arabic term 'taraduf' indicates successive transmission by many groups.
4
Reflect on the analogy
Nasafi likens the certainty from tawatur to our knowledge of famous generous Arabs like Hatim. Though we may not have certainty on each individual report, the collective testimony of many independent sources gives us assurance.
This analogy makes the abstract idea concrete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكمته. ولنبينا محمد عليه السلام من المعجزات الحسية ما لا يحصى كثرة، ذكرها نقلة الحديث وخلدوها في كتبهم وأعرضت عن ذلك مخافة التطويل. ثم وإن كان فيما ذكر أصحاب التواريخ ونقلة الأخبار والآثار أشياء نقلت على طريق الآحاد، وذلك لا يوجب العلم لكل فرد أنه حق لا محالة إلا أن ترادفها من أناس لا يتصور عليهم التواطؤ على الكذب، يكون دليلا على ظهور ما هو الناقض للعادة في الجملة على يديه، وإن لم يقع العلم بكل فرد كحكاية الأفراد عن وجود حاتم وكعب بن مامة وأبي داوود الإيادي وهرم بن سنان المري
His wisdom. And for our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, there are sensory miracles whose abundance cannot be counted; the transmitters of hadith mentioned them and recorded them in their books, and I refrained from that for fear of lengthiness. Then, even if among what the historians and transmitters of reports and traditions mentioned there are things transmitted via ahad (isolated) chains, and that does not necessitate certain knowledge for every individual that it is true without doubt, unless they are transmitted successively by people for whom collusion on lying is inconceivable, it is evidence for the occurrence of what breaks the custom in general at his hands, even if certain knowledge of each individual report is not attained, like the narration of individuals about the existence of Hatim, Ka‘b ibn Mamah, Abu Dawud al-Iyadi, and Hari, and Hari
Source pages p. 724

Commentary
This passage addresses the proof from miracles. The author first states that the Prophet's sensory miracles are too numerous to count and declines to list them for brevity. He then tackles a methodological issue: some reports of miracles are transmitted as ahad (single-chain) reports, which individually do not yield certain knowledge. However, he argues that if these reports are 'taradufa'—meaning they are reported by groups so numerous and diverse that collusion on falsehood is unimaginable—then they collectively prove that miracles (breaking of custom) occurred in general, even if each specific incident is not absolutely certain. He draws an analogy: just as we know of the existence of famous generous Arabs (Hat[] was moved to a new line? The Arabic cuts off at 'Hatim' — but the point is that general knowledge from multiple streams is reliable.) This is a classic argument for tawatur: multiple independent chains yield certainty even if individual chains are weak.

Key Terms
معجزات حسية (mu'jizat hissiyya)
آحاد (ahad)
ترادف (taraduf)
تواطؤ على الكذب (tawatu' 'ala al-kadhib)
ناقض العادة (naqid al-ada)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only mutawatir (mass-transmitted) reports can serve as proof; ahad reports are always insufficient.
Correction: Nasafi shows that ahad reports, when they reach the level of tawatur through multiple independent lines, collectively provide certain proof for the general occurrence of miracles.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, under what condition do ahad reports of miracles provide evidence for prophethood?
A) When they are recorded in books.
B) When they are transmitted by people for whom collusion on lying is inconceivable (tawatur).
C) When they are mentioned by historians.
D) When they are sensory miracles.

Key Takeaway
Ahad reports of miracles, when transmitted by so many independent groups that collusion is impossible, become proof for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the reports of the Prophet's miracles with the same level of certainty as you treat your knowledge of historical figures like Hatim? What does your answer reveal about the strength of your conviction?
?
If you were asked to defend the occurrence of the Prophet's miracles using Nasafi's argument, could you articulate it clearly from memory? What does that say about your ownership of this proof?
?
How often do you reflect on the sheer multiplicity of miracle reports about the Prophet? Will this lesson change how you receive ahad hadith about miracles—will you now be more confident or more cautious? What will you change starting today?

Understanding Tawatur Ma'nawi Through Analogies
Nasafi introduces tawatur ma'nawi via historical analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how individually uncertain ahaad reports can collectively produce certain knowledge via tawatur ma'nawi, as illustrated by the recognition of generosity and bravery in historical figures.

Core Idea
Many ahaad reports together can yield certainty, like knowing a person is generous from many isolated stories.

Before we can see how the Prophet's miracles are proven, we need a conceptual tool: tawatur ma'nawi. This lesson introduces the idea that many ahaad reports, each insufficient alone, can combine to produce certain knowledge—just as we know of Hatim's generosity or Antarah's bravery from scattered tales. Nasafi presents this analogy to ground his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Nasafi lists many names from Arab history before explaining the logic.
These names are not random; they are archetypes of generosity, bravery, and wisdom.
2
Grasp the problem and solution
Identify the problem: ahaad reports don't give certainty per se. Then see the solution: when many such reports come from different people who couldn't conspire, they prove the trait in general.
The key is 'لا يوجب العلم لكل فرد أنه حق... إلا أن ترادفها'.
3
Focus on the analogy mechanism
Nasafi says each story of generosity is ahaad, but together they prove the person was generous. Understand how this works without needing every story to be mutawatir.
This is the essence of tawatur ma'nawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكمته
ولنبينا محمد عليه السلام من المعجزات الحسية ما لا يحصى كثرة، ذكرها نقلة الحديث وخلدوها في كتبهم وأعرضت عن ذلك مخافة التطويل.
ثم وإن كان فيما ذكر أصحاب التواريخ ونقلة الأخبار والآثار أشياء نقلت على طريق الآحاد، وذلك لا يوجب العلم لكل فرد أنه حق لا محالة إلا أن ترادفها من أناس لا يتصور عليهم التواطؤ على الكذب، يكون دليلاً على ظهور ما هو الناقض للعادة في الجملة على يديه، وإن لم يقع العلم بكل فرد كحكاية الأفراد عن وجود حاتم وكعب بن مامة وأبي داوود الإيادي وهرم بن سنان المري والأجواد العشرة في صدر الإسلام، والبرامكة ومع ابن زائدة وغيرهم من الأجواد. وشجاعة عامر بن الطفيل وعتيبة بن الحارث بن شهاب، وبسطام بن قيس وعنترة بن شداد، وعمرو بن معد يكرب، وربيع بن عباد البكري، وحكمة أكثم بن صيفي وعامر بن الظرب وغير ذلك.
فإن حكاية كل فرد معنى من هذه المعاني عن المحكى عنه إن كان لا يوجب العلم بصحة تلك الحكاية بعينها فإنه يوجب العلم بكونه موصوفا بما وصف به في الجملة، فكانت كل حكاية في حق تلك الصورة التي وردت عنها في حيز الآحاد وهي بكليتها في حق أصل الجود والشجاعة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم حتى إن أحدًا لم يتردد في قلبه شك في جود من تقدم ذكره من الموصوفين بالجود، وكذا في شجاعة من مر ذكره، وكذا العلم والحكمة لما فكذا كل فرد من الأخيار في حق صورة ذلك المروى بعينه في حيز الآحاد ومجموعها في حق أنه كانت تظهر على يده المعجزات الناقضات للعادة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم بذلك.
وهذا معنى قول أهل الأصول إن الجزئيات المجوزة يتركب من مجوعها كلي موجب، ولسنا نعني أن كلا الشاة وشكاية الناقة وحنين الأسطوانة، وما ذكرنا نحن من قبيل هذا، بل كل واحد مما ذكرنا ثبت برواية قوم لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب.
His wisdom. And our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, had sensory miracles whose abundance cannot be counted. The transmitters of hadith mentioned them and recorded them in their books, but I refrained from that for fear of lengthening. Then, even if among what the historians and transmitters of reports and traditions have mentioned are things transmitted via ahaad (isolated) routes, and that does not necessitate knowledge for every individual that it is true without exception, unless they are successive from people for whom collusion on falsehood is inconceivable, it becomes evidence for the emergence of that which breaks the custom in general at his hands, even if knowledge of every individual (report) does not occur. Like the narration of individuals about the existence of Hatim, and Ka'b ibn Mamah, and Abu Dawud al-Iyadi, and Harm ibn Sinan al-Murri, and the ten generous ones in early Islam, and the Barmakids, and with Ibn Zaidah, and others among the generous. And the bravery of Amir ibn al-Tufayl, and Utaybah ibn al-Harith ibn Shihab, and Bistam ibn Qays, and Antarah ibn Shaddad, and Amr ibn Ma'dikarib, and Rabi' ibn Abbad al-Bakri, and the wisdom of Aktham ibn Sayfi and Amir ibn al-Zarib, and others. For the narration of each individual meaning of these meanings about the person narrated from, even if it does not necessitate knowledge of the correctness of that particular narration, it does necessitate knowledge that he is described by what he was described with in general. So each narration regarding that specific instance that it came about is in the realm of ahaad, yet collectively regarding the origin of generosity and bravery, it is in the realm of tawatur (mass transmission) that necessitates knowledge, so much so that no one hesitates in his heart with doubt about the generosity of those mentioned who are described with generosity, and likewise about the bravery of those whose bravery was mentioned, and likewise knowledge and wisdom. So too, every individual report of the righteous regarding the specific instance of that reported miracle itself is in the realm of ahaad, but their totality regarding the fact that miracles breaking custom appeared at his hands is in the realm of tawatur that necessitates knowledge of that. And this is the meaning of the statement of the scholars of usul: 'From the permitted particulars, there is composed a whole that is necessitating (of knowledge).' And we do not mean by that the splitting of the moon, the groaning of the camel, and the sighing of the pillar, and what we have mentioned ourselves is of this type; rather, each one of what we have mentioned is established by the narration of a people whose collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.
Source pages p. 724

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument proving that the Prophet's miracles are established with certainty despite many individual reports being ahaad (non-mass-transmitted). The author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, begins by stating that the Prophet's sensory miracles are too numerous to count, and he refrains from listing them to avoid making the work too long. He then addresses a potential scepticism: even if many reports of miracles are transmitted through ahaad chains (i.e., not reaching tawatur individually), they can collectively produce certain knowledge when the reports come from so many different people that collusion on falsehood is impossible. To illustrate this, he draws an analogy with well-known figures from Arab history known for generosity, bravery, or wisdom. For example, reports about the generosity of Hatim al-Ta'i or the bravery of Antarah are each ahaad, yet no one doubts that these individuals actually possessed those traits. Similarly, the many ahaad reports of different miracles performed by the Prophet—when considered together—compel knowledge that miracles did indeed occur. The author then clarifies that the tawatur in question is not tawatur of the exact wording (lafzi) but tawatur of meaning (ma'nawi). He explicitly excludes from this analogy such specific miracles as the splitting of the moon, the groaning of the camel trunk, or the sighing of the pillar (which are individually established by tawatur lafzi). Rather, the argument is about the aggregate of many ahaad reports that collectively yield certainty. He concludes by citing the usuli principle that 'from permissible particulars a necessitating universal is composed'—i.e., many contingent, individual reports can combine to yield certain knowledge of a general fact.

Key Terms
الآحاد
التواتر المعنوي
الجود
الشجاعة
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only tawatur lafzi (verbatim mass transmission) can give certain knowledge.
Correction: Nasafi demonstrates that tawatur ma'nawi—collective testimony of meaning—also yields certainty, as seen in the recognition of generosity from many ahaad stories.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why do we know with certainty that Hatim was generous, despite the stories being ahaad?
A) Each story is confirmed by the Quran.
B) The stories are so numerous and from different people that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.
C) The stories were directly witnessed by the Prophet.
D) The stories are all transmitted through the same chain.

Key Takeaway
Ahaad reports, when numerous and from irreconcilable sources, collectively produce certain knowledge of the general fact—this is tawatur ma'nawi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the mass of evidence for Islam's truth—accumulated from countless witnesses across centuries—as sufficient certainty for your faith, or do you still demand a single, individually verified proof for every detail? What would it take for you to stop hesitating in your heart?
?
When you hear isolated stories about the Prophet’s character or miracles, do you dismiss them as weak or do you let the cumulative weight of many such reports shape your conviction? How might your daily actions change if you truly believed that the overall picture is certain beyond doubt?
?
The passage says that no one doubts the generosity of Hatim al-Ta’i based on many ahaad reports. Is your knowledge of the Prophet's perfection as firm as that? If not, what is holding you back from that level of certainty, and what step will you take today to remove that barrier?

Miracles
intermediate
5 min
Applying Tawatur Ma'nawi to Prophetic Miracles
Nasafi applies tawatur ma'nawi to miracles and cites the usuli principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the concept of tawatur ma'nawi applies specifically to the Prophet's miracles, and how the usuli principle 'particulars compose a universal necessitating knowledge' supports this conclusion.

Core Idea
Individual ahaad miracle reports collectively force knowledge that the Prophet performed miracles.

Now that we grasp tawatur ma'nawi from the analogies, Nasafi directly applies it to the Prophet's miracles. He argues that countless ahaad reports of different miracles, each insufficient alone, together make it certain that miracles breaking custom appeared at his hands. He then cites a foundational usuli principle to formalize this reasoning, while clarifying that certain well-known miracles are established by tawatur lafzi, not this argument.

Guided Path
1
Apply the analogy to miracles
Read how Nasafi explicitly extends the logic: just as ahaad reports of generosity prove the trait, ahaad reports of miracles prove that miracles occurred.
The phrase 'فكذا كل فرد من الأخيار' signals the application.
2
Understand the usuli principle
Nasafi cites a maxim: 'From permissible particulars a necessitating universal is composed.' Grasp how this summarizes the argument: many contingent reports yield certain knowledge of a general fact.
This is a key methodological principle in Islamic epistemology.
3
Note the clarification
Nasafi distinguishes his argument from miracles like the splitting of the moon, which are established by tawatur lafzi. His point is about the collective weight of many diverse miracle reports.
This prevents confusion and shows the scope of his proof.

What does Nasafi mean when he says 'we do not mean by that the splitting of the moon, the groaning of the camel, and the sighing of the pillar'?
A) Those miracles are not real.

C) Those miracles are not accepted by all scholars.
D) Those miracles are not relevant to prophethood.

?

Your faith is at stake.
?

Are you avoiding that conclusion?

What is the state of your conviction regarding those specific miracles? Is it based on the strength of tawatur, or just habit? Commit to studying one such miracle report in detail this week.

The Principle of Collective Certainty from Ahad Reports
Principle: multiple ahad reports about a quality yield certain knowledge of that quality in general.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple isolated reports (ahad) about a quality combine to produce certain knowledge (tawatur) about that quality in general, without each report being certain individually.

Core Idea
Collective reports transform permissible particulars into a necessary universal.

Imam al-Nasafi tackles a key epistemological puzzle: if each single report about a person's generosity is uncertain in itself, how can we be certain that the person is generous? The answer lies in the cumulative effect of multiple reports. In this passage, he explains this principle using historical examples and cites the usul maxim that 'permissible particulars combine into a necessary universal'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two domains
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author distinguishes between the domain of ahad for specific instances and the domain of tawatur for the general quality.
The example of generosity and bravery illustrates this distinction clearly.
2
Understand the usul principle cited
Find the sentence where the author quotes the 'people of usul'. Reflect on the meaning: permissible particulars (which could be true or false) combine to form a necessary universal (certain knowledge).
This is the core theoretical takeaway.
3
Apply the principle to miracles
See how the author extends the same reasoning to the miracles of prophets. Each miracle report is ahad, but collectively they yield certain knowledge that miracles occurred.
This shows the principle's relevance to prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن حكاية كل فرد معنى من هذه المعاني عن المحكى عنه إن كان لا يوجب العلم بصحة تلك الحكاية بعينها فإنه يوجب العلم بكونه موصوفا بما وصف به في الجملة، فكانت كل حكاية في حق تلك الصورة التي وردت عنها في حيز الآحاد وهي بكليتها في حق أصل الجود والشجاعة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم حتى إن أحدًا لم يتردد في قلبه شك في جود من تقدم ذكره من الموصوفين بالجود، وكذا في شجاعة من مر ذكره، وكذا العلم والحكمة لما فكذا كل فرد من الأخيار في حق صورة ذلك المروى بعينه في حيز الآحاد ومجموعها في حق أنه كانت تظهر على يده المعجزات الناقضات للعادة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم بذلك. وهذا معنى قول أهل الأصول إن الجزئيات المجوزة يتركب من مجموعها كلي موجب، ولسنا نعني أن كلا الشاة وشكاية الناقة وحنين الأسطوانة، وما ذكرنا نحن من قبيل هذا، بل كل واحد مما ذكرنا ثبت برواية قوم لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب، فكان كل فرد من ذلك ثابتا بطريق التيقن كأنا عايناه، ولثبوته برواية من لا يتصور منهم التواطؤ على الكذب، وبالله التوفيق.
For the report of each individual meaning from these meanings about the reported person, if it does not necessitate knowledge of the correctness of that particular report, it nevertheless necessitates knowledge that he is described with what he was described with in general. So each report regarding that specific instance which came about is in the domain of ahad (isolated reports), while in its totality regarding the very basis of generosity and bravery it is in the domain of tawatur (mass transmission) that necessitates knowledge, to the extent that no one hesitates in his heart with doubt about the generosity of those previously mentioned who were described with generosity, and likewise about the bravery of those mentioned, and likewise knowledge and wisdom. Thus, every individual report about the righteous regarding the specific instance of that reported miracle is in the domain of ahad, but their totality regarding the fact that miracles breaking custom appeared at his hand is in the domain of tawatur that necessitates knowledge thereof. This is the meaning of the statement of the people of usul (principles): 'Permissible particulars combine from their totality into a necessary universal.' And we do not mean by this the talking wolf, the complaint of the camel, or the moaning of the pillar—what we have mentioned is not of this type. Rather, every single thing we mentioned is established by the transmission of a group for whom collusion upon lying is inconceivable. Thus, each individual instance is established with certainty as if we had witnessed it, due to its establishment by the transmission of those for whom collusion upon lying is inconceivable. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 725

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument. It explains how multiple isolated (ahad) reports about a quality (e.g., generosity, bravery) do not individually yield certainty about the specific instance, but collectively yield certain knowledge that the person possessed that quality in general. The author illustrates this with historical figures known for generosity and bravery. The same principle applies to miracles: individual reports of specific miracles are ahad, but their totality establishes with certainty that miracles occurred at the Prophet's hand. The author then cites the usul principle: permissible particulars combine into a necessary universal. He clarifies that this is not about legendary stories (talking wolf, etc.) but about reports from groups that cannot conspire to lie, thus producing certainty as if one witnessed it.

Key Terms
تواتر
آحاد
جزئيات مجوزة
كلي موجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every individual report must be certain in itself to produce knowledge.
Correction: Individual reports can be uncertain (ahad), but their combination yields certain knowledge (tawatur) about the general quality.

Checkpoint
What principle do the 'people of usul' use to explain how multiple individual reports produce certain knowledge?
A) A universal cannot be derived from particulars.
B) Permissible particulars combine from their totality into a necessary universal.
C) Isolated reports always remain in the domain of doubt.
D) Certain knowledge requires direct observation only.

Key Takeaway
Multiple ahad reports about a quality combine to produce certain knowledge (tawatur) of that quality, as encapsulated in the usul principle that permissible particulars yield a necessary universal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you truly gathered enough evidence from the Prophet's miracles to have certain faith in his prophethood? If not, what one specific miracle will you study this week to strengthen your certainty? Make a plan to read about it and reflect on how it contributes to the collective testimony.
?
The principle shows that many small pieces of evidence build undeniable certainty. In your own life, do you base your trust in Allah and His promises on multiple signs and verses, or only on one? Write down three signs from creation or from the Qur'an that together make you certain that Allah is with you. How will you recall them when you feel doubt?
?
If someone told you that the reports of the Prophet's miracles are just stories and not certain, how would you respond using the logic of this passage? Are you prepared to articulate this proof? If not, commit today to understanding it well enough to share with one person this week.

Distinguishing Reliable Miracle Reports from Legends
Clarification that the principle applies only to reports from groups that cannot collude on lies, not to legendary tales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the epistemological principle of collective certainty applies only to reports transmitted by groups that cannot collude on lies, not to legendary stories.

Core Idea
Certainty requires transmission by groups whose collusion on lies is inconceivable.

After explaining how multiple reports produce certain knowledge, Imam al-Nasafi clarifies that not every story qualifies. He explicitly distinguishes the miracle reports he refers to from legendary tales like a talking wolf or a moaning pillar. The key difference lies in the reliability of the transmitters: only reports from groups that could not possibly conspire to lie yield certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the clarification passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice that the author begins with a negation: 'We do not mean...' This sets up a contrast.
The examples (talking wolf, etc.) are legendary, not historical.
2
Identify the positive condition
The author states that the reliable reports are established by a group for whom collusion on lying is inconceivable. This is the condition for certainty.
Think about what makes a group incapable of colluding on lies: large numbers, diverse motivations, etc.
3
Reflect on the outcome
Because of this transmission, each individual report is as certain as if one had witnessed it. How does this compare to the earlier principle?
This shows that the principle works only when the transmission itself is reliable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن حكاية كل فرد معنى من هذه المعاني عن المحكى عنه إن كان لا يوجب العلم بصحة تلك الحكاية بعينها فإنه يوجب العلم بكونه موصوفا بما وصف به في الجملة، فكانت كل حكاية في حق تلك الصورة التي وردت عنها في حيز الآحاد وهي بكليتها في حق أصل الجود والشجاعة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم حتى إن أحدًا لم يتردد في قلبه شك في جود من تقدم ذكره من الموصوفين بالجود، وكذا في شجاعة من مر ذكره، وكذا العلم والحكمة لما فكذا كل فرد من الأخيار في حق صورة ذلك المروى بعينه في حيز الآحاد ومجموعها في حق أنه كانت تظهر على يده المعجزات الناقضات للعادة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم بذلك. وهذا معنى قول أهل الأصول إن الجزئيات المجوزة يتركب من مجموعها كلي موجب، ولسنا نعني أن كلا الشاة وشكاية الناقة وحنين الأسطوانة، وما ذكرنا نحن من قبيل هذا، بل كل واحد مما ذكرنا ثبت برواية قوم لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب، فكان كل فرد من ذلك ثابتا بطريق التيقن كأنا عايناه، ولثبوته برواية من لا يتصور منهم التواطؤ على الكذب، وبالله التوفيق.
For the report of each individual meaning from these meanings about the reported person, if it does not necessitate knowledge of the correctness of that particular report, it nevertheless necessitates knowledge that he is described with what he was described with in general. So each report regarding that specific instance which came about is in the domain of ahad (isolated reports), while in its totality regarding the very basis of generosity and bravery it is in the domain of tawatur (mass transmission) that necessitates knowledge, to the extent that no one hesitates in his heart with doubt about the generosity of those previously mentioned who were described with generosity, and likewise about the bravery of those mentioned, and likewise knowledge and wisdom. Thus, every individual report about the righteous regarding the specific instance of that reported miracle is in the domain of ahad, but their totality regarding the fact that miracles breaking custom appeared at his hand is in the domain of tawatur that necessitates knowledge thereof. This is the meaning of the statement of the people of usul (principles): 'Permissible particulars combine from their totality into a necessary universal.' And we do not mean by this the talking wolf, the complaint of the camel, or the moaning of the pillar—what we have mentioned is not of this type. Rather, every single thing we mentioned is established by the transmission of a group for whom collusion upon lying is inconceivable. Thus, each individual instance is established with certainty as if we had witnessed it, due to its establishment by the transmission of those for whom collusion upon lying is inconceivable. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 725

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument. It explains how multiple isolated (ahad) reports about a quality (e.g., generosity, bravery) do not individually yield certainty about the specific instance, but collectively yield certain knowledge that the person possessed that quality in general. The author illustrates this with historical figures known for generosity and bravery. The same principle applies to miracles: individual reports of specific miracles are ahad, but their totality establishes with certainty that miracles occurred at the Prophet's hand. The author then cites the usul principle: permissible particulars combine into a necessary universal. He clarifies that this is not about legendary stories (talking wolf, etc.) but about reports from groups that cannot conspire to lie, thus producing certainty as if one witnessed it.

Key Terms
تواطؤ على الكذب
اليقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The principle of collective certainty applies to any story, including legendary tales.
Correction: The principle only applies to reports transmitted by groups that cannot collude on lies, not to legendary stories that lack reliable transmission.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes the miracle reports the author refers to from legendary stories like the talking wolf?
A) The miracle reports are more famous.
B) They are transmitted by groups that cannot collude on lies.
C) They are from the Prophet himself.
D) They are mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Certainty from multiple reports requires that the transmitters are incapable of colluding on lies, which distinguishes reliable miracle accounts from legendary tales.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a religious story you have heard or believed without verifying its chain of transmission. Are you certain it meets the criteria of being transmitted by a group whose collusion on lies is inconceivable? How does that affect your certainty about that story?
?
When you hear a report about the Prophet (peace be upon him), do you usually ask about its reliability, or do you accept it based on emotion? What would it mean for your faith if you were to rely only on reports that meet the standard described in this passage?
?
This passage guards against being deceived by legendary tales. In your daily life, what sources of information do you accept without questioning their reliability? Are there any beliefs you hold that may have weak foundations? Consider the ultimate consequence of basing your deen on unverified reports.

The Four Main Categories of Intellectual Miracles
Enumeration of four main categories and subdivision of news into two.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four broad categories of the Prophet's intellectual miracles and the initial division of his prophetic news.

Core Idea
Intellectual miracles of the Prophet are classified into state, lineage, calls, and news.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi introduces a systematic classification of the Prophet's intellectual miracles. Rather than listing physical wonders, the author focuses on rational signs that affirm prophethood. The first part identifies four main categories: the Prophet's personal state, his lineage, his calls, and his news. The category of news is further divided into glad tidings in previous scriptures and his reports about future events.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's own classification come through.
Notice the concise style of enumeration.
2
Identify the four main categories
Find the four terms: state, lineage, calls, and news. Understand what each might refer to.
These are the broadest divisions.
3
Examine the subdivision of news
See how the news category is split into two: glad tidings from earlier scriptures and prophecies about future events.
This shows the variety of prophetic news.
4
Reflect on the significance of intellectual miracles
Ask yourself why the author emphasizes intellectual over sensory miracles. Consider their role in establishing prophethood rationally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما معجزاته العقلية فمنقسمة إلى أقسام فمنها ما هو راجع إلى حالة ومنها ما هو راجع إلى نسبه، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى دعواته، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى أخباره، وهذا ينقسم إلى قسمين: أحدهما ما ورد مع البشارات به في الكتب المتقدمة والأمم الماضية. والثاني: إخباره عن الكائنات، وهذا القسم الأخير ينقسم إلى قسمين: أحدهما: إخباره عن أمور ماضية. والثاني: إخباره عن أمور توجد في المستقبل ومنها معجزات ظهرت بعد وفاته عليه السلام، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى مكانه، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى زمانه، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى كتابه الذي أتى به، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى شريعته التي اختص بها. ونبين في كل فصل من هذه الفصول ما يوجب ثلج الصدر، ويسوق إلى القلوب برد اليقين، وإن ضاق عن ذلك صدر المتعنتين، ورغم أنف الملحدين الذين وصفهم الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله تعالى: فَإِنَّهُمْ لَا يُكَذِّبُونَكَ وَلَكِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ يَجْحَدُونَ.
As for His intellectual miracles, they are divided into categories: among them are those pertaining to his state, among them are those pertaining to his lineage, among them are those pertaining to his calls, and among them are those pertaining to his news. This last divides into two parts: one of them is what came with the glad tidings of him in the previous scriptures and past nations. The second is his informing about occurrences, and this last section divides into two parts: one of them is his informing about past matters, and the second is his informing about matters that will occur in the future. And among them are miracles that appeared after his death, peace be upon him, and among them are those pertaining to his place, and among them are those pertaining to his time, and among them are those pertaining to his book which he brought, and among them are those pertaining to his shari'a (law) which he exclusively possessed. And we will explain in each chapter of these chapters what causes the chest to be assured and leads to the hearts the coolness of certainty, even if the breasts of the obstinate are straitened by that and the noses of the atheists are humbled—those whom Allah Exalted described in His book by His saying: 'For indeed they do not disbelieve you, but the wrongdoers reject the signs of Allah.'
Source pages p. 726

Commentary
This passage is a classification and enumeration of the Prophet's intellectual miracles. The author divides them into main categories: those related to his state (ḥāla), lineage (nasab), calls (da‘awāt), and news (akhbār). The news category is further subdivided: glad tidings in previous scriptures, and his own prophecies about past and future events. Additionally, the author lists other categories: miracles after his death, related to place, time, his book (the Qur'an), and his shari'a. The passage concludes with a promise to explain each category in detail, stating that this will bring assurance and certainty, despite the obstinacy of disbelievers. The verse from Surah al-An‘am is cited to emphasize that rejection is due to injustice, not inability to recognize the truth.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intellectual miracles only refer to the Qur'an or physical events.
Correction: This passage shows a broader classification including personal state, lineage, calls, and various types of news.

Subdivisions of Prophetic News and Additional Categories
Further subdivision of news and listing of additional miracle categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the further subdivisions of prophetic news and the additional categories of intellectual miracles, including those related to time, place, the Qur'an, and Shari'a.

Core Idea
Prophetic news divides into past and future, and miracles also include those after death, related to place, time, the Qur'an, and Shari'a.

Imam al-Nasafi continues his classification by delving deeper into the category of prophetic news (akhbār). He divides it into reports about past events and reports about future events. Then he adds several more categories of intellectual miracles: those that appeared after the Prophet's death, those related to his place, his time, his book (the Qur'an), and his Shari'a. The passage concludes with a powerful statement about the certainty these miracles bring and a Quranic verse rebuking the obstinate.

The Miraculous Supplication of Prophet Yusuf
The author narrates the miracle of Prophet Yusuf's supplication causing drought and then rain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the supplication of Prophet Yusuf caused both drought and excessive rain, demonstrating the power of prophetic prayer as a miracle.

Core Idea
A prophet's supplication can control the elements as a sign of prophethood.

The passage opens with a narrative about Prophet Yusuf. When his people disobeyed, he prayed that rain be withheld, leading to a severe drought. Later, when they repented, he prayed for rain to return, and it came so abundantly that it destroyed houses. This story, transmitted by many chains, illustrates the miraculous nature of prophetic supplication and its role as a divine sign.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage carefully to understand the sequence of events: drought, prayer, rain, and the Prophet's second prayer to divert the rain.
Notice the phrase 'kullu dhalika manqulun bil-tawatur' emphasizing mass transmission.
2
Identify the two miraculous events
Find where the drought is mentioned and where the rain is mentioned. Both are results of Yusuf's supplication.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'tawatur'
Consider why the author stresses that these events are transmitted by tawatur. How does this strengthen the evidence for prophethood?
Tawatur means narration by so many that collusion is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوسف فأمسك عنهم القطر حتى جف النبات والشجر وهلكت المواشي. وكان انكشاف الجدب عنهم أيضًا بدعائه فأتاهم الغيث وكثر حتى هدم بيوتهم فكلموه في ذلك فقال : "اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا، اللهم على الظراب والجبال وبطون الأودية" وذلك كله منقول بالتواتر. ومن ذلك دعاؤه على كسرى حين مزق كتابه وبعث إليه بتراب فقال: "اللهم مزق ملكه كل ممزق". وقال لأصحابه: "مزق كتابي أما إنه ستمزق أمته، وبعث إلي بالتراب أما إنكم ستملكون أرضه". فمزق الله ملكه، وشتت جمعه، وملكهم أرضه. ومن ذلك دعاؤه على عتبة بن أبى لهب: "اللهم سلط عليه كلبًا من كلابك" فافترسه الأسد في بعض أسفاره، ومنها دعاؤه لعبد الله بن عباس بالفقه والحكمة فحصل ما دعا ومنها ما أعمى الله تعالى رضي الله عنهما أبصار الظالمين له حين كان في الغار ومنها ما ساخ بقوائم فرس من اتبعه في الأرض بدعائه، وفي ذلك كثرة، وفي هذا القدر كفاية.
Yusuf: He withheld from them rain until plants and trees dried and livestock perished. The removal of drought from them was also by his supplication, so rain came to them and increased until it destroyed their houses, and they spoke to him about that, so he said: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us; O Allah, on the hillocks, mountains, and valley bottoms.' All of that is transmitted by tawatur. Among that is his supplication against Kisra when he tore his letter and sent dust to him, saying: 'O Allah, tear apart his kingdom completely.' And he said to his companions: 'He tore my letter; indeed his nation will be torn apart. And he sent dust to me; indeed you will possess his land.' So Allah tore apart his kingdom, scattered his assembly, and gave them possession of his land. Among that is his supplication against Utbah ibn Abi Lahab: 'O Allah, set upon him a dog from Your dogs,' so a lion devoured him in one of his travels. Among them is his supplication for Abdullah ibn Abbas for jurisprudence and wisdom, and what he supplicated was realized. Among them is that Allah, may He be pleased with them both, blinded the eyesight of the oppressors to him when he was in the cave. Among them is that a horse's hooves sank into the ground for one who followed him by his supplication. There is much of this, and in this amount is sufficient.
Source pages p. 731

Commentary
This passage lists several miracles of the Prophet's supplications, demonstrating his prophethood. It begins with a story about Prophet Yusuf (Joseph) and a drought, but the focus is on the Prophet Muhammad's supplications. First, his prayer for rain brought relief, then his prayer against Kisra (the Persian king) led to the disintegration of his kingdom. Next, his prayer against Utbah ibn Abi Lahab resulted in him being killed by a lion. Then his prayer for Abdullah ibn Abbas granted him knowledge. Additionally, Allah blinded the enemies when the Prophet was in the cave, and a horse's legs sank into the ground in response to his supplication. The author states that all these are well-known through tawatur (mass transmission) and that this amount is sufficient as evidence.

دعاء
تواتر
معجزة
قطر
جدب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) He built dams to control the flood.
D) He migrated to another land.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Yusuf's supplication controlled the rain, proving his prophethood through a miracle transmitted by many narrators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Or do you rely only on material means? What would it take for you to call upon Him with full conviction, even when circumstances seem hopeless?
?

In your own prayers for relief from trials, do you ask with a similar concern for others' wellbeing? Can you recall a time when your dua included mercy for those who may have wronged you? What would change if you made such mercy a habit in your supplications?

Miracles of the Prophet Muhammad's Supplications
The author enumerates five miracles from the Prophet's supplications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand several miracles of Prophet Muhammad's supplications, including his prayers against enemies and for companions, as evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's supplications are miracles that confirm his prophethood.

The author continues by listing additional miracles of the Prophet's supplications, each transmitted by multiple narrators. These include his prayer against the Persian king Kisra, which led to the disintegration of his empire; his prayer against Utbah ibn Abi Lahab, resulting in his death by a lion; his prayer for Abdullah ibn Abbas to gain knowledge; the blinding of his enemies in the cave; and the sinking of a horse's legs by his prayer. Each demonstrates the divine power behind his words.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage to identify each miracle and its outcome. Notice the pattern: supplication followed by fulfillment.
The passage begins with 'wa min dhalika du'a'uhu 'ala Kisra'.
2
List the five miracles
Identify each miracle: prayer against Kisra, against Utbah, for Ibn Abbas, blinding of enemies, horse sinking.
3
Consider the role of tawatur
Although the word 'tawatur' is not repeated here, the previous passage set the context. Why is mass transmission important for these reports?
These events are part of the collective proof of prophethood.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Read the last sentence: 'wa fi hadha al-qadr kifayah'. What does the author imply about the sufficiency of these examples?
The author indicates that even this small selection is enough as evidence.

يوسف فأمسك عنهم القطر حتى جف النبات والشجر وهلكت المواشي. وكان انكشاف الجدب عنهم أيضًا بدعائه فأتاهم الغيث وكثر حتى هدم بيوتهم فكلموه في ذلك فقال : "اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا، اللهم على الظراب والجبال وبطون الأودية" وذلك كله منقول بالتواتر. ومن ذلك دعاؤه على كسرى حين مزق كتابه وبعث إليه بتراب فقال: "اللهم مزق ملكه كل ممزق". وقال لأصحابه: "مزق كتابي أما إنه ستمزق أمته، وبعث إلي بالتراب أما إنكم ستملكون أرضه". فمزق الله ملكه، وشتت جمعه، وملكهم أرضه. ومن ذلك دعاؤه على عتبة بن أبى لهب: "اللهم سلط عليه كلبًا من كلابك" فافترسه الأسد في بعض أسفاره، ومنها دعاؤه لعبد الله بن عباس بالفقه والحكمة فحصل ما دعا ومنها ما أعمى الله تعالى رضي الله عنهما أبصار الظالمين له حين كان في الغار ومنها ما ساخ بقوائم فرس من اتبعه في الأرض بدعائه، وفي ذلك كثرة، وفي هذا القدر كفاية.
Yusuf: He withheld from them rain until plants and trees dried and livestock perished. The removal of drought from them was also by his supplication, so rain came to them and increased until it destroyed their houses, and they spoke to him about that, so he said: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us; O Allah, on the hillocks, mountains, and valley bottoms.' All of that is transmitted by tawatur. Among that is his supplication against Kisra when he tore his letter and sent dust to him, saying: 'O Allah, tear apart his kingdom completely.' And he said to his companions: 'He tore my letter; indeed his nation will be torn apart. And he sent dust to me; indeed you will possess his land.' So Allah tore apart his kingdom, scattered his assembly, and gave them possession of his land. Among that is his supplication against Utbah ibn Abi Lahab: 'O Allah, set upon him a dog from Your dogs,' so a lion devoured him in one of his travels. Among them is his supplication for Abdullah ibn Abbas for jurisprudence and wisdom, and what he supplicated was realized. Among them is that Allah, may He be pleased with them both, blinded the eyesight of the oppressors to him when he was in the cave. Among them is that a horse's hooves sank into the ground for one who followed him by his supplication. There is much of this, and in this amount is sufficient.
Source pages p. 731

Commentary
This passage lists several miracles of the Prophet's supplications, demonstrating his prophethood. It begins with a story about Prophet Yusuf (Joseph) and a drought, but the focus is on the Prophet Muhammad's supplications. First, his prayer for rain brought relief, then his prayer against Kisra (the Persian king) led to the disintegration of his kingdom. Next, his prayer against Utbah ibn Abi Lahab resulted in him being killed by a lion. Then his prayer for Abdullah ibn Abbas granted him knowledge. Additionally, Allah blinded the enemies when the Prophet was in the cave, and a horse's legs sank into the ground in response to his supplication. The author states that all these are well-known through tawatur (mass transmission) and that this amount is sufficient as evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's supplications were answered by Allah, producing clear miracles that confirm his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Abdullah ibn Abbas was given unmatched knowledge through a single supplication. Have you ever honestly asked Allah to grant you deep understanding of your faith, or are you content with surface-level learning? What will you change today to seek knowledge with the same fervor as the Prophet’s companions?
?
The Prophet’s supplication caused a lion to devour his enemy. Are you aware that your own words can bring either blessing or destruction? Which of your habits or words do you need to repent from, knowing that Allah answers calls for help or harm?

Posthumous Miracles as Proof of Prophethood
Al-Nasafi gives examples of posthumous miracles proving the Prophet's truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles can occur after a prophet's death and serve as continuing evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Posthumous miracles confirm prophethood beyond a prophet's lifetime.

Al-Nasafi presents a series of remarkable events that occurred after the Prophet Muhammad's death, all serving as miracles (mu'jizat) that affirm his truth. These examples show that divine signs are not limited to his life but continue to manifest. This lesson examines these posthumous miracles and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without focusing on details. Then read the translation. Let the examples register.
The passage contains four distinct examples.
2
Identify the four examples
Find the four examples: the rain prayer, the martyrs of Badr, Talha's body, and Abu Ayyub al-Ansari's grave.
The first example is the most detailed.
3
Understand the miracle in each
For each example, note what makes it miraculous: the rain after prayer, the fresh bodies after decades, the dream causing exhumation, and the grave providing rain.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: Why does Al-Nasafi include these? They prove the Prophet's truth and honor even after his death.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[المعجزات التي ظهرت بعد وفاته] وأما ما ظهر من معجزاته وأعلامه بعد وفاته فكاستسقاء عمر بن الخطاب فإنه استسقى بالعباس بن عبد المطلب فسقوا حتى طفق الناس يمسحون أركان العباس ويقولون: هنيئًا لك ساقي الحرمين، وهذا مشهور تفتخر به بنو العباس. ومن ذلك إخراج شهداء بدر رطابا بعد خمسين سنة وهو أمر مشهور بالمدينة، وكذا قصة طلحة حين رأته ابنته عائشة في المنام فقال لها يا بنية حوليني من هذا المكان فقد أضرني الندى، فأخرجته بعد ثلاثين سنة وحولته وهو طري لم يتغير، وتولى إخراجه عبد الرحمن بن سلامة الكندي. ومن ذلك أن أبا أيوب الأنصاري حين مات بقسطنطينية فقبر عند سور المدينة وبنى عليه، فكانوا إذا أمحلوا
And as for what appeared of his miracles and signs after his death, such as the prayer for rain of Umar ibn al-Khattab, for he sought rain through al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib, and they were given rain until people began wiping the corners of al-Abbas and saying: 'Congratulations to you, water-carrier of the two sanctuaries.' This is famous and the Banu Abbas boast of it. And among that is the bringing out of the martyrs of Badr fresh after fifty years, which is a well-known matter in Medina. Likewise the story of Talha when his daughter Aisha saw him in a dream, and he said to her: 'O my daughter, move me from this place, for dampness has harmed me.' So she brought him out after thirty years and moved him while he was moist and unchanged. Abd al-Rahman ibn Salamah al-Kindi carried out the exhumation. And among that is that Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, may God be pleased with him, when he died in Constantinople, was buried at the wall of the city and a structure was built over it, and whenever they suffered drought
Source pages p. 740

Commentary
This passage presents posthumous miracles (mu'jizat ba'd al-wafat) that prove the Prophet's truth. Al-Nasafi gives three examples: First, Umar's prayer for rain through al-Abbas, which resulted in rain and the people honored al-Abbas. Second, the bodies of the martyrs of Badr were exhumed after fifty years and found fresh and unchanged. Third, the body of Talha ibn Ubaydullah was exhumed after thirty years, still moist and unchanged, as his daughter Aisha dreamt of him complaining of dampness. The fourth example is of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari's grave in Constantinople, which served as a source of rain when the people suffered drought. These events are presented as miracles that demonstrate the Prophet's continued honor and truth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles only occur during a prophet's lifetime.
Correction: Al-Nasafi provides examples of posthumous miracles that also confirm prophethood.

Checkpoint

B) The prayer for rain by Umar through al-Abbas.
C) The ascension to heaven.
D) The revelation of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Posthumous miracles, such as the rain prayer and preserved bodies of companions, serve as ongoing proof of the Prophet's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The companions' bodies remained moist and unchanged for decades. What does that teach you about the worth of their sacrifice? Are you willing to sacrifice something for this faith, even if you don't see immediate reward?

Posthumous Miracles: The Rain Prayer of Umar through al-Abbas
Nasafi cites the rain prayer of Umar through al-Abbas as a posthumous miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the miracle of rain through al-Abbas after the Prophet's death serves as a posthumous prophetic miracle.

Core Idea
Posthumous miracles affirm the Prophet's prophethood even after his death.

Imam Nasafi begins his enumeration of posthumous miracles with a famous event from the caliphate of Umar. When drought struck, Umar prayed for rain through al-Abbas, the Prophet's uncle, and rain was granted. This event became a source of pride for the Banu Abbas. In this lesson, we examine this miracle and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the details of the story: the drought, Umar's prayer through al-Abbas, and the people's reaction.
Pay attention to the phrase 'هنيئًا لك ساقي الحرمين' which shows the honor given to al-Abbas.
2
Reflect on the role of al-Abbas
Consider why Umar chose al-Abbas as an intermediary. This highlights the virtue of the Prophet's family and the continuation of his blessings.
3
Connect to prophethood
Understand that this miracle is attributed to the Prophet, as it happened after his death but through his uncle. It serves as a sign of his prophethood.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعجزات التي ظهرت بعد وفاته
وأما ما ظهر من معجزاته وأعلامه بعد وفاته فكاستسقاء عمر رضي الله عنه فإنه استسقى بالعباس رضي الله عنه فسقوا حتى طفق الناس يمسحون أركان العباس ويقولون: هنيئًا لك ساقي الحرمين، وهذا مشهور تفتخر به بنو العباس. ومن ذلك إخراج شهداء بدر رطابا بعد خمسين سنة وهو أمر مشهور بالمدينة، وكذا قصة طلحة حين رأته ابنته عائشة في المنام فقال لها يا بنية حوليني من هذا المكان فقد أضرني الندى، فأخرجته بعد ثلاثين سنة وحولته وهو طري لم يتغير، وتولى إخراجه عبد الرحمن بن سلامة الكندي. ومن ذلك أن أبا أيوب الأنصاري رضي الله عنه حين مات بقسطنطينية فقبر عند سور المدينة وبنى عليه، فكانوا إذا أمحلوا كشفوا عن قبره فمطروا، وكل كرامة ظهرت لولي ففيها معجزة النبي عليه السلام على ما نبين - إن شاء الله.
Miracles that appeared after his death. As for what appeared of his miracles and signs after his death, such as the rain-seeking prayer of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, for he sought rain through al-Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, and they were watered until people began wiping the corners of al-Abbas and saying, 'Congratulations to you, waterer of the two sanctuaries.' This is famous and the Banu Abbas boast of it. Among that is the bringing out of the martyrs of Badr fresh after fifty years, and that is a well-known matter in Medina. Likewise the story of Talha when his daughter Aisha saw him in a dream and he said to her, 'O my daughter, move me from this place, for the moisture has harmed me.' So she brought him out after thirty years and moved him while he was fresh, unchanged. His exhumation was undertaken by Abd al-Rahman ibn Salama al-Kindi. Among that is that Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, may Allah be pleased with him, when he died in Constantinople, was buried at the city wall and a structure was built over him. When they suffered drought, they would uncover his grave and be given rain. And every miracle (karama) that appears from a saint (wali) contains a miracle (mu'jiza) of the Prophet, peace be upon him, as we will explain, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 740

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of posthumous miracles of the Prophet, followed by a general principle. The Imam lists three examples: First, Umar's rain-seeking prayer through al-Abbas, which brought rain and caused people to honor al-Abbas. Second, the exhumation of the martyrs of Badr after fifty years, found fresh. Third, the story of Talha's body remaining fresh after thirty years, as seen in a dream by his daughter. Fourth, the grave of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari being a source of rain during drought. The passage concludes with the principle that every miracle (karama) of a saint is in fact a miracle (mu'jiza) of the Prophet, because it attests to his prophethood. The phrase 'as we will explain' indicates that this is a preview of a fuller discussion.

Key Terms
معجزة
استسقاء
العباس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That posthumous miracles are independent events unrelated to the Prophet's prophethood.
Correction: Nasafi shows this miracle is a sign of the Prophet's prophethood, as it occurred through his uncle and is counted among his miracles.

Checkpoint

B) Because it happened after the Prophet's death and through his uncle.
C) Because al-Abbas was a virtuous man.
D) Because the people were happy.

Key Takeaway
Umar's rain prayer through al-Abbas is a posthumous miracle that validates the Prophet's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Posthumous Miracles: Fresh Corpses and the Link to Prophethood
Nasafi lists three posthumous miracles and states the general principle linking saintly miracles to the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three additional posthumous miracles and the principle that every saint's miracle contains a prophetic miracle.

Core Idea
Every miracle of a saint is a continuation of the Prophet's miracle.

Nasafi continues with more examples: the bodies of Badr martyrs and Talha preserved fresh for decades, and the grave of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari bringing rain. He concludes that all such miracles are tied to the Prophet's miracle. This lesson explores these events and their doctrinal implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the three stories
Read the passage which narrates three distinct miracles: the fresh bodies of Badr martyrs after 50 years, the fresh body of Talha after 30 years seen in a dream, and the grave of Abu Ayyub providing rain.
Notice the common theme: freshness and provision of rain.
2
Identify the common thread
All three miracles involve life-like preservation or blessing from graves. Reflect on how these attest to the Prophet's truth.
3
Grasp the concluding principle
Nasafi states that every saintly miracle (karama) contains a prophetic miracle (mu'jiza). This is the doctrinal takeaway: saints' miracles are not independent but derive from the Prophet.
This directly addresses a potential misconception.
