The Poetry Challenge: Exposing Nazzam's Obstinacy
Poetry challenge to expose obstinacy and argument from differentiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses a practical poetry challenge to expose the falseness of Nazzam's claim that anyone could produce the Quran without divine prevention.

Core Idea
Inability to produce great poetry reveals Nazzam's obstinacy.

The author opens by declaring Nazzam's argument false and corrupt. Instead of a theoretical rebuttal, he issues a direct challenge: produce a poem like those of the greatest Arab poets. This practical test exposes Nazzam's obstinacy and sets the stage for a rational argument based on the known differentiation among people in eloquence.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening refutation
Start by reading the passage where the author labels Nazzam's speech as false and corrupt. Notice the tone of certainty.
2
Understand the challenge
The author lists specific famous poems by Imru' al-Qais, an-Nabigha, etc. Ask yourself: why these specific examples? They set an unambiguous standard of eloquence.
The challenge is meant to be impossible to meet if Nazzam's theory were false.
3
Analyze the dilemma
The author poses a dilemma: either Nazzam could produce such poetry but chose inferior ones (absurd), or he cannot. The only logical conclusion is his inability.
4
Connect to differentiation
The author argues that if Nazzam were right, there would be no difference between poets and common speakers, but this differentiation is known by intuition. This shows Nazzam's argument leads to absurdity.
This step shows the argument is not just rhetorical but based on self-evident truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا منه كلام باطل واحتجاج فاسد، فإن أقرب ما يجاب عنه أن يقال: ائت بقصيدة مثل قصيدة امرئ القيس: قفا نبك، أو مثل قصيدته: ألا انعم صباحا أيها الطلل البالي، أو مثل قصيدته خليلي مرا بي على أم جندب أو مثل قصيدته: شمالك شرق بعدما كان أقصر، وغيرها من القصائد له ولغيره من فحول الشعراء كالنابغة وطرفه وزهير والأعشى ليظهر عند عجزه عن ذلك أنه مكابر فيما يقول، ويقال له: متى عجزت أنت أعند التكلم بالكلمة الأولى أو عند التكلم بالكلمة الأخرى؟ أهل عصرك كصريع الغواني ومروان بن أبي حفصة وأبي نواس وسلم الخاسر وأشجع السلمى وغيرهم في نهاية الجودة والبلاغة ورشاقة النظم وجزالة الألفاظ وإحكام الصنعة؟ ألأنك مع القدرة على مثل تلك القصائد البليغة الفصيحة المحكمة اخترت لنفسك الأدون والأرذل والأبشع؟ أم لأنك عجزت عن ذلك، ولم ينقد لطبعك البارد الثقيل مثل تلك القصائد؟ ولا يخفى على أحد أن ذلك كان لعجزه عن اختياره، وكذا ما ذكر يؤدي إلى ارتفاع التفاضل بين الشعراء والخطباء والبلغاء والفصحاء وانعدام الإفحام، وحيث كان التفاضل بين هؤلاء معلومًا وانقسام الناس إلى الشعراء المعلقين والمتبلدين المفحمين أمرا ظاهرا دل أن ذلك كلام باطل يعرف بطلانه ببديهة العقل. وما ذكر من الحجة يوجب بطلان ما عرف ثبوته بطريق الضرورة، وهو ما ذكرنا من التفاضل بين النظم، وانقسام الناس إلى الشعراء وأهل الإفحام، وكل استدلال عرف بطلانه ضرورة كان باطلا، لما أن الخطأ على الاستدلال جائز الضروري ممتنع، فكان عند التعارض إضافة الخطأ إلى ما كان الخطأ فيه جائز أولي من إضافته إلى ما كان الخطأ فيه ممتنعا. ثم نقول ما ذكرت من اعتبار الجمل بالأفراد مقدمة كاذبة وقضية مجحودة، دلالة كذبها ما آنفا مر من قدرة كل من الناس على كل فرد من أفراد كلمات القصائد الفصيحة والخطب البليغة، وعجزهم عن جمل القصائد والخطب. ثم نقول: أليس أن الرجل يعجز عن حمل ألف رطل، وكل رطل من ذلك
This from him is false speech and corrupt argument. For the nearest answer to him is to say: Produce a poem like Imru' al-Qais's poem: 'Qifa nabki', or like his poem: 'Ala an'am sabahan ayyuha at-talal al-bali', or like his poem: 'Khalilayya murra biya 'ala Ummi Jundab' or like his poem: 'Shimaluka sharqun ba'da ma kana aqsar', and other poems by him and by other master poets like an-Nabigha, Tarafa, Zuhayr, al-A'sha, so that when you fail it becomes clear that you are being obstinate in what you say. And it is said to him: When did you fail – at speaking the first word or at speaking the other word? The people of your time like Sari' al-Ghawani, Marwan ibn Abi Hafsa, Abu Nuwas, Salm al-Khasir, Ashja' as-Sulami and others at the peak of quality, eloquence, grace of composition, grandeur of words, and perfection of craftsmanship? Is it that while having the ability to produce such eloquent, eloquent, well-crafted poems, you chose for yourself the lower, more vile, and uglier? Or is it that you failed in that, and your cold, heavy nature did not yield such poems? And it is not hidden from anyone that that was due to his inability to produce them. Similarly, what he mentioned leads to the elimination of differentiation among poets, orators, eloquent speakers, and the disappearance of refutation. And since differentiation among these is known, and the division of people into poets who are eloquent and dullards who are refuted is obvious, it indicates that that is false speech whose falsehood is known by rational intuition. And what he mentioned of the argument necessitates the falsehood of what is known to be established by necessary knowledge, namely what we mentioned of the differentiation in composition and the division of people into poets and those who are refuted. And every inference whose falsehood is known necessarily is false, because error in inference is possible, while error in necessary knowledge is impossible. Thus, when there is conflict, attributing error to what is possible is more appropriate than attributing it to what is impossible. Then we say: What you mentioned of considering the whole based on the parts is a false premise and a rejected proposition. The proof of its falsehood is what we have already mentioned: that every person has the ability to produce each individual word of eloquent poems and eloquent speeches, but they are unable to produce the entire poems and speeches. Then we say: Is it not that a man is unable to carry a thousand pounds, while each pound of that…
Source pages p. 751

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of an-Nazzam's theory of sarfa. The author begins by declaring Nazzam's speech false and corrupt. The nearest answer is a practical challenge: Nazzam is asked to produce a poem comparable to those of the great pre-Islamic and Islamic poets like Imru' al-Qais, an-Nabigha, etc. If he cannot, his claim that anyone could produce the Quran without divine prevention is exposed as obstinacy. The author then turns Nazzam's own part–whole argument against him: just as a person can speak individual words but cannot compose an eloquent poem, so too the Quran's parts are not miraculous individually, but the whole composition is. The author further argues that the existence of clear differentiation (tafadul) between poets and common speakers is known by necessity (darura). Since Nazzam's argument leads to denying this self-evident fact, his argument must be false. The passage then rejects the part–whole premise as false, giving the analogy of carrying a thousand pounds – a person can lift each pound individually but not all together. This illustrates that the whole can have a different ruling than the parts. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the thrust is clear: Nazzam's reasoning is invalid.

التفاضل
الإفحام
بديهة العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The author shows that the Quran's inimitability is proven by the inability of poets to match it, even without divine prevention.

The argument from differentiation relies on rational intuition (badihah al-‘aql). Do you trust your God-given reason to recognize clear truths, or do you sometimes separate faith and intellect? How can you more fully integrate rational reflection into your daily walk with Allah starting today?

The Part–Whole Argument: Rejecting Nazzam's False Premise
Refutation of Nazzam's part-whole premise using empirical proof and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the part–whole analogy (like carrying a thousand pounds) to refute Nazzam's claim that the Quran's inimitability is only due to divine prevention.

Core Idea
The whole can be greater than its parts; inability to compose a poem does not refute the Quran's miracle.

In the second part of the refutation, the author directly addresses Nazzam's part–whole argument. Nazzam had argued that since a person can produce individual words similar to the Quran, they could produce the whole Quran. The author rejects this premise as false and gives a clear analogy: a man can lift each pound of a thousand-pound load but cannot lift the whole. This shows that the whole has a different property than its parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the rejection of the premise
Read the passage where the author calls Nazzam's part-whole premise false and rejected. Notice the language of certainty.
2
Examine the empirical proof
The author reminds that every person can produce individual words of eloquent poems but cannot compose the entire poem. This is presented as a clear fact.
3
Understand the analogy
The author asks: is it not that a man is unable to carry a thousand pounds, though he can carry each pound? This illustrates that the whole can be greater than the sum of its parts.
The analogy is meant to be intuitive and universally understood.
4
Apply to the Quran
Consider how the same logic applies to the Quran: individual words are not miraculous, but the entire composition is. Nazzam's false premise collapses.
This connects back to the earlier point about differentiation.

The Analogy of Carrying a Thousand Pounds
Autor presents a logical analogy to refute denial of miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a simple analogy about weightlifting refutes an argument against miracles by exposing a logical contradiction.

Core Idea
Inability to do a large task does not mean inability to do its parts.

The author presents a logical analogy to show that denying the miraculous nature of the Quran leads to an absurd contradiction. By comparing the impossibility of carrying a thousand pounds to the possibility of carrying each pound individually, he exposes the flaw in the opponent's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author sets up the analogy: a man cannot carry a thousand pounds but can carry each pound.
2
Identify the two alternatives
The passage presents two possible responses from the opponent: admit the analogy (invalidating his proof) or deny one part of it (leading to obstinacy). Find both alternatives.
3
Reflect on why denial is obstinate
Consider why rejecting either part of the statement is irrational. The author labels such denial as stubbornness (كابر وعاند). Think about how this refutes the opponent's original argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : أليس أن الرجل يعجز عن حمل ألف رطل، وكل رطل من ذلك مقدور الحمل؟ فإن أقر بذلك أبطل دليله وإن جحد أحد شطري هذا الكلام بأن قال: حمل ألف رطل وعشرة آلاف رطل وأزيد من ذلك مقدور لمن كان له حمل كل رطل منه مقدوراً، أو قال : لما لم يكن حمل ألف رطل مقدورًا لأحد لا يكون حمل رطل مقدوراً له، فقد كابر وعاند.
Then we say: Is it not that a man is unable to carry a thousand pounds, while each pound of that is capable of being carried? If he acknowledges that, he invalidates his proof; and if he denies one of the two parts of this statement by saying: 'Carrying a thousand pounds and ten thousand pounds and more than that is possible for one for whom carrying each pound of it is possible,' or he says: 'Since carrying a thousand pounds is not possible for anyone, then carrying a pound is not possible for him,' then he has acted obstinately and stubbornly.
Source pages p. 753

Commentary
This passage presents a logical refutation directed at an opponent who denies the miraculous nature of the Quran by arguing from general human incapacity. The author uses an analogy about a man unable to carry a thousand pounds even though he can carry each individual pound. If the opponent admits that inability to carry a large weight does not negate the ability to carry its parts, he undermines his own proof. If he denies this and asserts either that carrying the whole is possible if the parts are possible, or that inability for the whole implies inability for the parts, then he is guilty of obstinate contradiction. The argument aims to show that the opponent's reasoning is internally inconsistent.

Key Terms
عجز
قدرة
معاندة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that inability to do a large task implies inability to do its components.
Correction: The analogy shows that inability for a composite task does not negate ability for its individual parts. The opponent's denial of this is obstinate.

Checkpoint

A) That the opponent's argument is consistent.
B) That the opponent is obstinate if he rejects either part of the analogy.
C) That carrying a thousand pounds is always possible.
D) That the opponent admits his proof is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The opponent's denial of the analogy forces him into irrational obstinacy, thereby refuting his argument against miracles.

The Dilemma of Sarfah: Choice or Compulsion?
Objection against the doctrine of sarfah using a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma posed against the doctrine of sarfah (turning away) and its implications for the doctrines of free will and divine obligation.

Core Idea
The sarfah doctrine traps its proponents between two impossible positions.

This passage presents a powerful objection against the Mu'tazilite doctrine of sarfah—the claim that God turned people away from producing a match to the Qur'an. The author forces the opponent to confront a dilemma: either the turning away happens by the servant's choice or by compulsion, both of which contradict key Mu'tazilite principles. Then, he pushes further, showing that if sarfah is permitted, it leads to an inconsistency with the doctrine of al-aslah (the most beneficial).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the argument flow.
Pay attention to the logical structure.
2
Identify the two options
The opponent is given two choices: by choice or by compulsion. Note why both are impossible for him.
These options are mutually exclusive and both are denied by the Mu'tazilite.
3
Trace the further objection
If the opponent deviates and accepts sarfah, then why does God not turn away disbelievers from disbelief? This leads to a second dilemma.
This involves the doctrine of al-aslah (the most beneficial).
4
Understand the conclusion
The opponent is left with two contradictory positions, invalidating sarfah and al-aslah.
The argument is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال له : ما معنى صرف هممهم عن المعارضة ؟ أفعل ذلك باختيار من العبد أم لا باختياره؟ فإن قال : فعل ذلك باختيار من العبد، فهذا منه إثبات التصرف لله تعالى في الأفعال الاختيارية للعباد وتعليق قدرته بها، وهذا عنده محال، وإن فعل باضطرار من العبد، فقد أثبت الله تعالى منع قدرة العبد عما يختار من الأفعال، وهذا عنده محال ، ثم لو خالف أهل نحلته وجوز ذلك قيل له: إذا كان ذلك جائزا فلم لا يصرف همة الكافر عن الكفر وهمة العاصي عن المعصية لئلا يقع في ذلك إذ هو أصلح له، والله تعالى يجب عليه فعل الأصلح عندك؟ فإذا لم يفعل ذلك فأنت بين طرفي نقيض فإما أن تقول : لم يفعل لأنه لم يقدر وهذا يبطل القول بالصرفة، وإما أن تقول: إنه وإن قدر لم يفعل ذلك في حق الكافر والعاصي، وفيه بطلان قولك بالأصلح.
Then it is said to him: What is the meaning of 'turning away their efforts from producing a match'? Did that happen by the choice of the servant or not by his choice? If he says: 'It happened by the choice of the servant,' then this from him is an affirmation of God's disposal in the voluntary actions of servants and the attachment of His power to them, and this is impossible according to him. And if it happened by compulsion from the servant, then he has affirmed that God prevents the power of the servant from whatever he chooses of actions, and this is impossible according to him. Then, if he opposes the people of his sect and permits that, it is said to him: If that is permissible, then why does He not turn away the effort of the disbeliever from disbelief and the effort of the sinner from sin so that he does not fall into it, since that is more beneficial for him? And God must do what is more beneficial according to you? So if He does not do that, then you are between two contradictory positions: either you say He did not do it because He was not able, and this invalidates the doctrine of sarfah (turning away), or you say that although He was able, He did not do that in the case of the disbeliever and sinner, and in that is the invalidation of your statement about the more beneficial.
Source pages p. 753

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the doctrine of sarfah—the claim that God turned people away from producing a match to the Quran. The author asks: Did this turning away happen by the servant's choice or by compulsion? If by choice, then it implies God's power intervenes in voluntary acts, which the opponent denies. If by compulsion, then God prevents the servant's power, also denied by the opponent. Then the author pushes further: if the opponent deviates from his sect and accepts sarfah, then why does God not turn away disbelievers and sinners from evil, since it is more beneficial for them? This leads to a dilemma: either God is unable (invalidating sarfah) or He is able but does not act, which contradicts the opponent's doctrine of al-aslah (the most beneficial). Thus the opponent is trapped between two contradictory positions.

Key Terms
صرفة
اختيار
اضطرار
أصلح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sarfah is a neutral, unproblematic concept.
Correction: The passage shows that sarfah leads to contradictions regarding free will and divine obligation.

Checkpoint
What is the first dilemma posed to the opponent regarding the meaning of 'turning away'?
A) Either it is by choice or by compulsion, both of which the opponent denies.
B) Either it is a miracle or a natural phenomenon.
C) Either it happens to all or only to some.
D) Either it is voluntary or involuntary, and the opponent accepts both.

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of sarfah is self-defeating because it forces its proponents to choose between contradicting their own principles or facing an inconsistency with al-aslah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God has complete power over your choices? When you sin, do you ever blame God for not turning you away? This lesson shows that such a view leads to contradictions. How will you take full responsibility for your actions today, knowing God does not force you?
?
When you see someone reject faith despite clear evidence, do you doubt God's goodness or power? This passage challenges the idea that God must force belief. Can you trust that God's wisdom in allowing disbelief is greater than your understanding of what is 'most beneficial'? What does that trust require of you?
?
The dilemma of sarfah reveals that human logic cannot fully grasp God's actions. Are you willing to submit to God's will even when it seems contradictory to your sense of justice? What is one area of your life where you need to surrender your own reasoning and trust God's decree?

Why the Claim of Lost Quranic Matches Fails
Refutation of the claim that matches to the Quran disappeared due to Islam's power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument that valid matches to the Quran existed but have been lost due to the power of early Muslims is logically unsound and historically contradicted.

Core Idea
If matches existed, enemies would have preserved them; their absence proves impossibility.

Some opponents of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) have claimed that they did produce speeches matching the Quran, but that these were lost because Islam's early followers suppressed them. This lesson examines the logical and historical flaws in that claim, using the author's own argument and the example of Musaylima's surviving nonsense.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its refutation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the claim and the immediate refutation. The author calls it 'excessive ignorance.'
Notice the structure: objection, then refutation, then proof.
2
Follow the logical argument
The author uses a conditional argument: if the opponents had matched the Quran and were more powerful, they would have preserved their matches. Since they didn't, the claim is false.
The key point: the opponents' motive and power would have ensured transmission.
3
Analyze the example of Musaylima
The author cites Musaylima's nonsense as a counterexample: despite Muslim power, his texts survived. This disproves the idea that Muslim power erases counter-texts.
Compare: if Musaylima's poor imitations remain, why would a real match disappear?
4
Reflect on the lesson's implication
Understand that the Quran's preservation and unmatched nature is a sign of its divine origin. The failure to produce any preserved match is evidence.
This ties back to the broader discussion of miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن زعم الجاحدون لرسالته أنهم عارضوه إلا أن ذلك صار مندرسًا لعلو كلمته وشيوع دعوته وشدة شوكة أتباعه وأشياعه. قيل لهم هذا جهل مفرط، فإنهم لو عارضوه وكان المنكرون له أكثر من متبعيه وأعداؤه أوفر عددًا وأقوى يدًا من أوليائه؛ لكان ينبغي أن ينقل أولئك المعارض كما نقل هؤلاء القرآن إذ كانت حاجتهم إلى ذلك ماسة لدفع خصومهم من ألا ترى أن ما أتى به مسيلمة الكذاب من الهذيان كيف بقى وما هاجموا به رسول الله لم يرتفع ولم ينعدم لكثرة أعوان الإسلام وأنصاره، وقوة أشياع النبي وأتباعه.
If the deniers of his messengerhood claim that they matched it, but that became effaced due to the highness of his word, the spread of his call, and the intense power of his followers and partisans, it is said to them: This is excessive ignorance. For if they had matched it and the deniers of him were more numerous than his followers and his enemies more abundant in number and stronger in hand than his allies, then it would have been necessary that those matches be transmitted just as these people transmitted the Quran, since their need for that was pressing to repel their opponents. Do you not see that what Musaylima the liar brought of nonsense—how it remained, and what they attacked the Messenger of Allah with did not disappear nor become nonexistent due to the abundance of the helpers of Islam and its supporters, and the strength of the partisans of the Prophet and his followers?
Source pages p. 753

Commentary
This passage refutes the objection that the Quran was indeed matched by opponents but those matches were lost because of the overwhelming power of Islam's early supporters. The author calls this claim 'excessive ignorance.' He argues logically: if the opponents had actually produced a match, they would have had a strong motive to preserve it to refute the Prophet, especially since they were more numerous and powerful. Since they did not preserve it, the claim is false. The author cites the counterexample of Musaylima the liar, whose nonsensical 'revelations' survived despite the strength of the Muslims. This shows that powerful opposition does not cause the erasure of texts; rather, the fact that no valid match has been preserved proves its impossibility.

Key Terms
مندرِس
مسيلمة
عارض
حاجة ماسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the lack of preserved matches to the Quran is due to historical suppression by Muslims.
Correction: The author argues that if matches existed, opponents (who were more powerful) would have preserved them. Moreover, Musaylima's texts survived, showing that suppression did not happen.

Checkpoint
What example does the author use to show that powerful supporters do not erase counter-texts?
A) The poetry of pre-Islamic poets.
B) The nonsense of Musaylima the liar.
C) The books of Ibn al-Rawandi.
D) The arguments of the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
The claim that valid matches to the Quran were lost due to Muslim power is logically self-defeating and historically contradicted by the survival of Musaylima's texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are you willing to let this logical proof settle any doubts in your heart, or do you still harbor reservations? What would that say about your trust in Allah's preservation?
?
Musaylima's nonsense survived despite the strength of Islam. This proves that even weak counter-texts are preserved. How does this historical fact challenge any hidden assumptions you might have about the superiority of material power over truth? Are you willing to examine your own trust in worldly strength versus divine proof?
?

What is at stake for your own faith if you were to accept that claim? Will you commit to memorizing this argument to defend the Quran's miracle when needed?

Refuting the Fear Excuse for Not Matching the Quran
Refuting the fear excuse by logical and historical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that fear of Muslims prevented opponents from producing a match to the Quran, using logical consistency and historical examples.

Core Idea
Fear is not the reason — Ibn al-Rawandi wrote against Islam despite the risk.

The source passage tackles a common objection: that opponents of Islam could not produce a match to the Quran because they feared the sword of Muslims. The author dismantles this excuse by pointing out that such opponents already openly deny the Prophet and risk death, so their fear is inconsistent. He then cites historical figures who wrote anti-Islamic works despite the danger, proving that fear alone did not prevent a challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the argument flow.
Notice the rhetorical style: the author directly addresses the opponent.
2

The opponents already openly deny the Prophet and face death for that, so producing a match is no greater risk. Their fear is not a valid excuse.
This is the core of the refutation.
3
Examine the historical examples
Ibn al-Rawandi and Ibn Zakariyya al-Mutatabbib wrote books attacking Islam, showing that fear of the sword did not deter them.
These examples illustrate that the real obstacle is the Quran's inimitability.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author proves that the excuse of fear is baseless; the lack of a match is due to the Quran's miraculous nature, not fear.
Connect this to the broader doctrine of i'jaz (inimitability).

This passage is a refutation of the claim that opponents could not produce a match to the Quran because they feared the sword of Muslims. Refutation of the Fear Excuse for the Quran's Inimitability
Argument that failure to challenge Qur'an stems from inability, not fear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that the Qur'an's opponents failed to produce a challenge not from fear but from genuine inability, supported by historical examples of heretics who openly attacked Islam without fear yet produced no rival text.

Core Idea
Opponents failed to challenge the Qur'an not from fear, but because they simply could not.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi refutes the claim that the Arabs refrained from challenging the Qur'an out of fear of persecution. He points out that many heretics openly composed works attacking Islam yet never produced a text comparable to the Qur'an. This lesson traces his argument and considers its implications for understanding the Qur'an's inimitability.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the full translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument.
The passage is long but cohesive; try to grasp the overall structure.
2
Identify the central claim and anticipated objection
Notice that the author first addresses opponents directly, then anticipates the objection that they feared the sword of believers. Look for how he counters this.
The objection is that fear prevented them, not inability.
3
Analyze the historical examples
The author lists several heretics (Ibn al-Rawandi, al-Razi, etc.) who openly wrote against Islam without fear. Ask yourself: why does this prove the point?
These individuals had the motivation and opportunity but still produced no literary challenge.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the real reason is their inability, which makes the proof binding. Consider how this establishes the Quran's inimitability.
The passage ends with a new objection, but the main argument is complete at 'فلزمتهم الحجة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ألا ترى أن ما أتى به مسيلمة الكذاب من الهذيان كيف بقى وما هاجموا به رسول الله لم يرتفع ولم ينعدم لكثرة أعوان الإسلام وأنصاره، وقوة أشياع النبي وأتباعه. ثم نقول لهم: أنتم لن يعوزكم الكتبة البلغاء والخطباء والفصحاء، وفضلتم سادة العرب بضمكم إلى فصاحة العرب أنواع العلوم واشتغالكم بدرسها طول عمركم، وإحرازكم حكمة الهند وفلسفة اليونان وسياسة العجم، ثم أنتم المخاطبون بقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِّثْلِهِ ﴾ مطالبون بذلك محجوجون به، فأتوا أنتم بمثله وعارضوه بشكله، فإن زعمتم أنكم تخافون الحفاظ للملة الذابين عنها بالسيوف والرماح والعامة المتسارعين إلى إراقة الدماء من عرفوا منه القدح في الدين الذي يدينون به. قيل لكم ما لكم تجاسرتم على إظهار المخالفة وبسط اللسان في الرسول بالتكذيب، وفي الحجة بالجحود والرد واستحقاقكم القتل واستيجابكم إراقة الدماء به لا بإظهار ما يعارض الحجة ويقابل الدليل ؟ فإن قلتم : إنا نظهر المقالة سراً. قيل لكم: فأظهروا المعارض أيضا سرا. ثم نقول ما بال ابن الراوندي لم تمنعه هيبة الذابين عن الدين الناصرين له عن تصنيف كتاب التاج، وكتاب الزمرد وقضيب الذهب، وابن زكريا المتطبب لم يمنعه من ذلك عن تصنيف كتاب مخاريق الأنبياء وكتاب نقض الأديان، وجماعة التنويه بالبصرة لم يمنعه من تصانيف لهم كثيرة في نصرة قولهم بأصلين قديمين للعالم والطعن في الإسلام بل عن المجاهرة في المناظرة والمقابلة لدى المجادلة والاسفراري لم يمنعه ذلك عما صنف من أنواع الإلحاد وجماعة الباطنية لم يمنعهم ذلك عما صنفوا من الكتب لنصرة نحلتهم الرديئة وثلبهم الدين الظاهر كأبي حاتم الرازي والكوسج البزدوي والجاورساني وأبي علي وغيرهم ممن يطول ذكرهم حتى اشتهر كل ذلك، وانتشر في أداني بلدان الإسلام وأقاصيها، وبلغ جميع أطراف الأرض ونواحيها، والخلعاء والمجان لم يمنعهم ذلك من هجو الإسلام وشهر رمضان والصيام والصلاة وأشباه ذلك ومنعهم عن المعارضة وهي أشفى لصدورهم، وأشد تحصيلاً لفرضهم ومقصودهم، بل امتنعوا عن ذلك لعجزهم وقصورهم، فلزمتهم الحجة وانقطعت معذرتهم في الإعراض عنه ؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، عجزوا عن ذلك لأنه كان أفصحهم لسانًا وأجودهم بيانًا على ما روى عنه عليه السلام أنه قال: "أنا أفصح العرب"، وذلك لا يدل
Do you not see how the raving that Musaylima the Liar brought remained, and what they attacked the Messenger of Allah with did not disappear or cease due to the abundance of supporters of Islam and its helpers, and the strength of the followers and adherents of the Prophet? Then we say to them: You are not lacking in eloquent scribes, orators, and speakers; and you have surpassed the masters of the Arabs by combining with the eloquence of the Arabs the various sciences, and your occupation with studying them all your life, and your acquisition of the wisdom of India, the philosophy of the Greeks, and the politics of the Persians. Then you are the ones addressed by His statement, the Exalted: 'Then bring a surah like it,' required by it and argued against by it. So bring something like it and oppose it with its like. If you claim that you fear the protectors of the faith, who defend it with swords and spears, and the common people who rush to shed blood from those known to have reviled the religion they follow, it is said to you: How is it that you have dared to manifest opposition and to extend your tongues in denial of the Messenger, and in denial and rejection of the proof, making yourselves deserving of killing and deserving of the shedding of your blood by that, but not by manifesting something that opposes the proof and confronts the evidence? If you say: We manifest the statement secretly, it is said to you: Then manifest the opposition secretly as well. Then we say: What is the matter with Ibn al-Rawandi? The awe of the protectors of the religion and its helpers did not prevent him from composing the book 'al-Taj', 'al-Zumurrud', and 'Qadhib al-Dhahab'. And Ibn Zakariyya the physician was not prevented by that from composing the book 'Mukhariq al-Anbiya' and the book 'Naqd al-Adyan'. And the group in Basra were not prevented from many compositions of theirs in support of their statement that the world has two eternal principles, and from reviling Islam, even from open disputation and confrontation in debate. And al-Isfarari was not prevented by that from what he composed of various types of heresy. And the group of the Batiniyya were not prevented by that from the books they composed to support their vile sect and their reviling of the outward religion, such as Abu Hatim al-Razi, al-Kusaj al-Bazdawi, al-Jawarsani, Abu Ali, and others whose mention is lengthy, until all that became famous and spread throughout the near and far lands of Islam, and reached all the ends and regions of the earth. And the scoundrels and the insane were not prevented by that from satirizing Islam, the month of Ramadan, fasting, prayer, and the like, but they were prevented from producing an opposition, which would have been more satisfying to their hearts and more effective in achieving their desire and purpose. Rather, they refrained from that due to their inability and deficiency, so the proof became binding upon them and their excuse for turning away from it was cut off. If they say: Yes, they were incapable of that because he was the most eloquent of them in tongue and the best of them in clear expression, according to what is narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he said: 'I am the most eloquent of the Arabs,' and that does not indicate...
Source pages p. 754

Commentary
This passage is an extended argument for the miraculous nature of the Quran, specifically its inimitability (i'jaz). The author refutes the claim that the Arabs' failure to produce a similar text was due to fear of punishment rather than inability. The argument proceeds in several steps: First, the author points out that even when the early Muslims were fewer, the nonsense of Musaylima persisted, while attacks on the Prophet did not succeed. Then he addresses the opponents directly, noting that they possess eloquence, learning from multiple civilizations, and are specifically challenged by the Quranic verse to produce a surah like it. He anticipates the objection that they fear the sword of the protectors of Islam and the zeal of the common people. He counters this by asking why, then, they openly express their opposition and denial, which itself warrants death, yet they do not produce a counter-text—which, if successful, would be a more powerful blow. They could do so secretly, as they allegedly express their opposition secretly. The author then provides historical evidence: Ibn al-Rawandi, Ibn Zakariyya (al-Razi), the Basran materialists, al-Isfarari, the Batiniyya (with named individuals), and the vilest of people openly composed works attacking Islam without fear, yet none produced a challenge to the Quran. This shows that fear is not the reason; rather, inability prevents them. The passage ends with the objection that the Prophet's own superior eloquence made them incapable, and the author begins to refute this, but the argument is cut off.

تحدي
معارضة
عجز
إعجاز القرآن
فصاحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The author shows that many heretics openly attacked Islam without fear, yet none produced a similar text, proving that the real reason was inability.

Checkpoint

D) Because they were not skilled in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's inimitability is established by the opponents' inability to produce a similar text despite having the motivation, opportunity, and lack of fear, as demonstrated by historical heretics.

The opponents openly blasphemed and attacked Islam in many ways, but they could not produce a literary challenge. If the worst enemies of Islam couldn't produce a text like it, what does that say about your own excuses? ?

Three Aspects of the Quran's Miraculousness
Imam al-Nasafi enumerates three aspects of the Quran's i'jaz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct aspects of the Quran's miraculousness (i'jaz) as presented by Imam al-Nasafi: foreknowledge of the unseen, comprehensive wisdom in rulings, and extraordinary conciseness containing vast knowledge.

Core Idea
The Quran's i'jaz has three dimensions: foreknowledge, wisdom, and conciseness.

Imam al-Nasafi, in this passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla, presents a multi-faceted argument for the miraculous nature of the Quran. He identifies three distinct aspects that demonstrate its divine origin, moving beyond mere linguistic eloquence to include knowledge of the unseen, perfect wisdom, and incredible conciseness. This lesson will walk through each aspect, showing how the Quran's content could not have been produced by a human, especially an unlettered prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three aspects
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author explicitly enumerates three aspects. Highlight each one as you find it.
The listing is introduced by 'من أوجه ثلاثة' (from three aspects).
2
Examine the first aspect: knowledge of the unseen
Focus on the first aspect: the Quran contains predictions of future events until the Day of Judgment. Reflect on why this is considered miraculous — only Allah knows the unseen.
This aspect emphasizes divine omniscience.
3
Analyze the second and third aspects
The second aspect is the comprehensive wisdom in all rulings, beyond human capacity. The third is the conciseness of the Quran — a small book containing knowledge that would fill thousands of volumes. Consider how these prove the Quran's divine origin.
These aspects highlight perfect wisdom and power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكون، ويعلم وجه الحكمة والصواب في كل ذلك، ليودع ذلك كله الكتاب، فكان فيه الإعجاز من أوجه ثلاثة: أحدها العلم بما يكون في المستقبل إلى قيام الساعة، وهو علم الغيب لا يعلمه إلا الله تعالى. والثاني: العلم بوجه الحكمة والمصلحة في كل ذلك، وليس في طباع البشر أن يعلم رجل أمي لم ينفق عمره في إحراز العلوم واكتساب الآداب والحكم وجهة الحكمة والصواب والمصلحة في حوادث أسبوع واحد لإنسان واحد من جنس واحد فضلا عن جميع أجناس الحوادث الواقعة في العبادات، وأنواع المعاملات والمواريث والمعاشرات لجميع العالم إلى آباد الدهر، فعلم أن ذلك ورد من عند علام الغيوب الذي لا يعزب عنه شيء ولا يخفى عليه خافية. والثالث: أنه ليس في مقدور البشر أن يودع في واحد منهم في مقدار دفتر من الكتاب ما يربو من العلوم عند التفتيش والإيضاح والبسط على ألف دفتر وزيادة، فدل أن ذلك بالقادر الذي لا يصعب عليه أمر ولا يعجزه شيء، والله الموفق.
It is, and He knows the aspect of wisdom and correctness in all of that, so that He might deposit all of that in the Book. Thus in it there is miraculousness from three aspects: The first: knowledge of what will be in the future until the establishment of the Hour, and it is knowledge of the unseen which none knows except Allah the Exalted. The second: knowledge of the aspect of wisdom and benefit in all of that, and it is not in the nature of humans that an unlettered man who has not spent his life acquiring sciences and gaining etiquettes and wisdoms should know the aspect of wisdom, correctness, and benefit in the events of one week for one human from one genus, let alone for all genera of events occurring in acts of worship, and types of transactions, inheritances, and social interactions for the entire world unto endless ages. So it is known that that came from the Knower of the Unseen from whom nothing escapes and no secret is hidden. The third: that it is not within the capacity of humans that any one of them should deposit in the amount of a notebook of a book what amounts, upon investigation, clarification, and expansion, to a thousand notebooks and more. So that indicates that it is from the Powerful for whom no matter is difficult and nothing incapacitates Him. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 757

Commentary
This passage enumerates three aspects of the Quran's miraculousness (i'jaz). The first aspect is predictive knowledge of future events until the Day of Judgment, which is knowledge of the unseen known only to Allah. The second aspect is the comprehensive wisdom and benefit contained in the Quran's rulings, which an unlettered prophet could not have produced through human effort. The third aspect is the conciseness of the Quran: a small volume contains knowledge that would require thousands of volumes to explain fully. These three aspects prove that the Quran is from the All-Knowing and All-Powerful God.

Key Terms
إعجاز
أوجه ثلاثة
علم الغيب
الحكمة والمصلحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think i'jaz is solely linguistic.
Correction: This lesson shows that i'jaz also includes knowledge of the unseen, comprehensive wisdom, and extraordinary conciseness.

Checkpoint
How many aspects of the Quran's miraculousness does the author mention?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Quran's miraculousness is proven through its foreknowledge, comprehensive wisdom, and extraordinary conciseness, all beyond human capacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that the Quran contains comprehensive wisdom for all transactions and social interactions (المعاملات والمَعَاشِرَات). In which area of your daily life have you been relying on human wisdom rather than consulting the Quran? Will you commit to turning to the Quran for guidance in that area starting today?
?
The Quran is so concise that it contains knowledge that would fill thousands of volumes if expanded. Does your engagement with the Quran reflect the belief that every single verse carries immense depth? If not, what will you change in your approach to reading even one verse this week?
?
Knowing that the Quran predicts the unseen until the Day of Judgment, including the ultimate accountability, how does that reshape your priorities? Are there actions you are putting off that you would do if you truly believed the Hour could come at any moment? What concrete step will you take to live with that certainty?

The Mu'tazila Denial of Karamat: A Self-Refuting Argument
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila denial of karamat using their lack of them as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the Mu'tazila's own deprivation of karamat as evidence against their denial of miraculous gifts for the righteous.

Core Idea
Denying karamat is self-refuting: the Mu'tazila's lack of them proves their error.

Nasafi presents a powerful argument against the Mu'tazila denial of karamat by turning their own piety against them. He notes that despite their devotion and caution, no karamat appear among them, which itself indicates the corrupt state of their beliefs. This passage highlights the spiritual consequence of false creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the tone of certainty and the use of reported karamat among the early generations.
2
Identify Nasafi's evidence
Find the key argument: the Mu'tazila are deprived of karamat despite their apparent diligence in worship. This is the core evidence against them.
Notice the phrase 'حرمانهم الكرامة' (their deprivation of karamah).
3
Reflect on the spiritual implication
Consider why deprivation of karamat is a sign of falsehood. Nasafi connects it to their corrupt beliefs making them enemies of Allah, deserving humiliation.
The physical description of their appearance (pale, ugly complexion) is a spiritual sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد روى في التابعين والصالحين من الكرامات ما لا يدخل تحت الإحصاء بحيث يدخل منكرها في جملة منكري العيان. وأنكرت المعتزلة ذلك لأنهم حرموا ذلك لشؤم بدعتهم، ولو لم يكن على بطلان مذاهبهم وفساد عقائدهم دليل سوى حرمانهم الكرامة مع جدهم واجتهادهم في العبادات وشدة توقيهم عن المعاصي والآثام خوفًا من خروجهم عن الإيمان، ثم لم يكن يظهر على أحد منهم كرامة، ولم يعاين أحد منهم ذلك في نفسه ليرجع عنه ويعود إلى الإقرار به، ولم يكن ذلك إلا لبقائهم بسبب عقائدهم الفاسدة أعداء الله تعالى مستحقين للإهانة فيرى الأكثر منهم وقد تعلوهم صفرة سمجة تنبو الأبصار عن النظر إلى طلعته، وتثقل على القلوب معاشرته وصحبته.
And it has been narrated about the followers (tabi'un) and the righteous that there are karamat (miraculous gifts) beyond enumeration, such that its denier enters into the group of those who deny the obvious. And the Mu'tazila denied that because they were deprived of it due to the ill omen of their innovation. And if there were no evidence for the falsity of their doctrines and the corruption of their beliefs except their deprivation of karamat despite their seriousness and diligence in worship and their intense caution against sins and transgressions for fear of exiting from faith, then no karamah appeared from any of them, nor did any of them witness it in himself to recant and return to acknowledging it. And that was not except due to their corrupted beliefs, making them enemies of Allah, deserving of humiliation. So you see most of them with a pale, ugly complexion that hurts the eyes to look at, and whose company and companionship weigh heavily on hearts.
Source pages p. 782

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position that denies karamat (miraculous gifts for saints). The author begins by noting that ample karamat have been reported from the early generations, to the point that denying them is like denying the obvious. Then he states that the Mu'tazila denied karamat due to their bad innovation. He argues that even if there were no other evidence against them, the fact that they were deprived of karamat despite their sincere worship (as they claim) and caution against sin is itself a sign of the corruption of their beliefs. He notes that no karamah appeared among them, nor did they witness one in themselves to bring them back to belief. This shows that due to their corrupt beliefs, they are enemies of Allah deserving of humiliation. He then describes their appearance as having a pale, ugly complexion that repels others, indicating the spiritual effect of their false beliefs.

معتزلة (Mu'tazila)
بدعة (bid'ah)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying karamat is just a minor difference of opinion and does not affect one's faith.
Correction: Nasafi argues that denying karamat is a grave error that stems from corrupt beliefs, as evidenced by the Mu'tazila's own deprivation of such gifts despite their apparent piety.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's deprivation of karamat despite their outward piety proves the corruption of their beliefs and serves as a sign of their spiritual state.

Karamah of a Wali as a Miracle for the Prophet
Nasafi defends karamah as evidence for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a wali's karamah serves as evidence for the truth of the prophet's message and does not invalidate miracles.

Core Idea
A saint's miracle confirms the prophet's message.

Nasafi here addresses a key objection: if saints can perform extraordinary acts, doesn't that undermine the uniqueness of prophetic miracles? He argues the opposite—every karamah actually strengthens the proof of prophethood because it shows the truth of the beliefs the saint follows. Let's trace his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the heading and the argument that follows.
The passage is a response to the Mu'tazila claim.
2
Identify the opposing view
Find where Nasafi states the claim he is refuting: that karamat invalidate prophetic miracles.
3
Understand the central argument
Nasafi explains that a karamah shows the wali is correct in his belief, and since he follows a prophet, it confirms that prophet's truth. Follow this chain.
4
Notice the criticism of opponents
Nasafi accuses those who disagree of speaking without reflection, failing to use the intellect as a criterion.
5
Reflect on the role of intellect
Consider why Nasafi emphasizes using the intellect to distinguish truth from falsehood in this matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كرامة الولي معجزة للرسول] إنكاره، وما زعموا أن ظهورها على يدي الأولياء يوجب بطلان معجزات الأنبياء عليهم السلام، فكلام من يتفوه بما يخطر بباله من غير التأمل والتروي والعرض على العقل الذي هو القانون الذي بشهادته يمتاز [؟] الحق من الباطل، والصحيح من الفاسد، وذلك لأنه لو تأمل لعرف أن كل كرامة لولي معجزة للرسول عليه السلام فإن بظهورها يعلم أنه ولي وكونه وليًا على كونه محقا في عقيدته وهو فيها تابع لرسول مقر برسالته دليل على صحة رسالته، فكان ذلك على هذا التدريج دليلاً على صدق الرسول فيما ادعاه من الرسالة وبلغ من الدين والشريعة، فمن جعل ما هو معجزة للرسول ودلالة صدقه مبطلاً للمعجزة وسادًا لطريق الوصول إلى معرفتها فهو في غاية الجهل والغباوة.
[The statement that] the karamah of a wali is a miracle for the prophet — his denial of it. And what they claimed that its appearance at the hands of the awliya (saints) necessitates the invalidation of the miracles of the prophets, peace be upon them, is the speech of someone who speaks whatever comes to his mind without reflection, deliberation, and presentation to the intellect, which is the criterion by whose testimony the truth is distinguished from falsehood, and the correct from the corrupt. That is because if he reflected, he would know that every karamah of a wali is a miracle for the prophet, peace be upon him, for by its appearance it is known that he is a wali and that being a wali indicates that he is correct in his belief. And since he is in that a follower of a prophet, affirming his message, it becomes evidence for the truth of the message. Thus, this is, in this way, evidence for the truth of the messenger in what he claimed of prophethood and conveyed of religion and law. So whoever makes what is a miracle for the prophet and a proof of his truthfulness into something that invalidates the miracle and blocks the way to knowing it is in the utmost ignorance and stupidity.
Source pages p. 782

Commentary
This passage is a direct response to the Mu'tazila claim that karamat of saints would invalidate the miracles of prophets. The author begins with the heading that the karamah of a wali is a miracle for the prophet, then states that their claim is baseless speech without reflection. He argues that if they reflected, they would realise that every karamah of a wali supports the prophet's miracle because the wali's karamah proves that he is a true wali, and his being a wali is based on following the prophet and affirming his message. This, in turn, confirms the truth of the prophet's message. So far from invalidating miracles, the karamah actually serves as evidence for them. He concludes by saying that whoever thinks otherwise is extremely ignorant and dull-witted.

Key Terms
كرامة (karamah)
معجزة (mu'jizah)
ولي (wali)
رسول (rasul)
عقل (intellect)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The extraordinary acts of saints (karamat) invalidate the miracles of prophets because they are similar in nature.
Correction: Nasafi argues that karamat actually confirm prophetic miracles because they demonstrate the truth of the beliefs of the saint, who is a follower of the prophet.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how does a wali's karamah relate to the prophet's miracle?
A) It is separate and independent.
B) It is a miracle for the prophet, confirming his truth.
C) It invalidates the prophet's miracle.
D) It is only for the wali's own benefit.

Key Takeaway
A saint's karamah confirms rather than negates the miracle of the prophet he follows.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The passage says the intellect is the criterion to distinguish truth from falsehood. Distinction Between Mu'jizah and Karamah
Nasafi lists distinguishing features of mu'jizah vs karamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key features that distinguish the miracle of a prophet (mu'jizah) from the miracle of a saint (karamah), including the role of claim, concealment, and protection.

Core Idea
Mu'jizah is proclaimed, karamah is concealed; the saint fears istidraj, the prophet is protected.

In this lesson, Imam al-Nasafi addresses a common confusion: How can we tell apart the miracle of a prophet (mu'jizah) from the gift of a saint (karamah)? He provides several clear criteria, from the context of the miracle to the attitude of its recipient. Understanding these distinctions helps us avoid theological errors and appreciate the different roles of prophets and saints.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the categories
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview. Notice that the heading mentions four terms: mu'jizah, karamah, ma'unah, and ihana, but the discussion focuses on distinguishing the first two.
Pay attention to how the passage starts with a rhetorical question.
2
Identify the first two distinguishing features
Focus on the sentences about claiming prophethood and claiming sainthood. A mu'jizah appears after a claim of prophethood; if a wali (saint) claimed prophethood, he would become an unbeliever. Also, if a wali claims sainthood, he loses it immediately.
This shows that the context of the miracle matters: prophets openly claim a role, while saints do not.
3
Contrast display versus concealment
The prophet displays his miracle openly, while the saint strives to conceal his karamah, fearing it might be istidraj (gradual entrapment). The saint also pleads for secrecy if others become aware.
This difference in attitude is a key practical marker.
4
Consider divine protection
The prophet is ma'sum (protected) from altering the miracle, while the saint is not guaranteed such protection. This ensures the miracle remains intact for its prophetic purpose.
This final point ties the distinction back to the unique role of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الفرق بين المعجزة والكرامة والمعونة والإهانة] ثم نقول : وكيف يؤدي ذلك إلى التباس الكرامة بالمعجزة، والمعجزة تظهر على أثر دعوى الرسالة، ولو ادعى الولي الرسالة لكفر من ساعته، وصار عدوا الله لا يظهر على يده نقض العادة البتة، ولو ادعى الولاية تسقط عنه الولاية عند دعواه إياها، وكذا صاحب المعجزة لا يكتم معجزته بل يظهرها، وصاحب الكرامة يجتهد في كتمانها ولا يركن في الأغلب إليها، ويخاف أنها من قبيل الاستدراج له دون الكرامة، ولو اطلع الله تعالى أحدًا من صالحي عباده على كرامة الولي لتشفع إليه الولي وطلب بغاية التضرع أن يكتم ذلك عليه ولا يفشيه خوفا من الاغترار لدى الاشتهار، وكذا صاحب المعجزة مأمون العاقبة معصوم عن التبديل والولي بخلافه.
[The difference between the miracle (mu'jizah), the saintly gift (karamah), divine assistance (ma'unah), and humiliation (ihana)] Then we say: How does that lead to confusion between karamah and mu'jizah? The mu'jizah appears after the claim of prophethood. If the wali claimed prophethood, he would become an unbeliever immediately and become an enemy of Allah; a breaking of custom would never appear at his hands. And if he claimed sainthood (wilayah), his sainthood is removed from him when he claims it. Likewise, the possessor of a mu'jizah does not conceal his miracle but displays it, while the possessor of a karamah strives to conceal it and generally does not rely on it, fearing that it might be a form of gradual entrapment (istidraj) rather than a karamah. And if Allah informs one of His righteous servants about the karamah of a wali, the wali would intercede and ask with the utmost humility to keep it hidden and not disclose it, for fear of delusion from fame. Likewise, the possessor of a mu'jizah is secure in outcome and protected from alteration, while the wali is not.
Source pages p. 783

Commentary
This passage is a classification and distinction between mu'jizah (the miracle of a prophet), karamah (the miracle of a saint), and also ma'unah (divine assistance) and ihana (humiliation) mentioned in the heading. The author begins by asking how confusion could arise between karamah and mu'jizah. He then gives several differentiating features: (1) Mu'jizah occurs after a claim of prophethood; if a wali claimed prophethood he would become an unbeliever. (2) If a wali claims sainthood, he loses it. (3) The prophet displays his miracle openly, while the saint conceals his karamah, fearing it might be istidraj (gradual luring into sin). (4) If others become aware of a saint's karamah, the saint pleads for it to be kept secret to avoid pride. (5) The prophet is protected (ma'sum) from altering the miracle, while the saint is not guaranteed that protection. Thus, karamah and mu'jizah are clearly distinct.

Key Terms
معجزة (mu'jizah)
كرامة (karamah)
معونة (ma'unah)
إهانة (ihana)
ولي (wali)
رسول (rasul)
استدراج (istidraj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that the miracles of saints (karamah) and the miracles of prophets (mu'jizah) are identical and can be confused without distinction.
Correction: Nasafi shows they are clearly different: mu'jizah is tied to a claim of prophethood, displayed openly, and the prophet is protected from alteration; karamah is concealed, feared as istidraj, and the saint is not protected.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a distinguishing feature of a mu'jizah according to Nasafi?
A) It is concealed by its owner.
B) It appears after a claim of prophethood.
C) It is feared to be istidraj.
D) The owner pleads for it to be kept secret.

Key Takeaway
Mu'jizah and karamah are distinguished by the presence of a prophetic claim, open display, and divine protection, while karamah is marked by concealment, fear of istidraj, and lack of protection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you do a good deed, do you secretly hope it gets noticed? What would it take for you to truly conceal it out of fear that it might be a form of istidraj rather than a genuine honor from Allah?
?
If you were told that a miracle had occurred through you, would you be quick to share it or would you beg Allah to keep it hidden? What does that reveal about your attachment to fame and your fear of delusion?
?
The prophet is protected from altering his message. You are not. In what areas of your religious practice do you feel most vulnerable to self-deception, and how does this lesson's distinction between mu'jizah and karamah make you more cautious about your own spiritual experiences?

The Benefit of Karamat
Nasafi explains the benefits of karamat despite objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple benefits of karamat and how they serve both the saint and the wider purpose of confirming prophethood.

Core Idea
Karamat have profound benefits beyond mere wonder.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses a common objection that the miracles of saints (karamat) are pointless. He first dismisses the objection by noting that lack of understanding does not invalidate reality. Then he enumerates several concrete benefits that karamat provide, showing their spiritual and doctrinal significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the argument's flow.
2
Identify the objection and Nasafi's initial response
Note the objection that karamat have no benefit. Observe how Nasafi first responds by saying ignorance of the wisdom does not invalidate the reality.
This is a key methodological point: lack of understanding is not a proof of falsehood.
3
List the five benefits
Find the five benefits Nasafi lists after 'Then we say:' (ثم نقول). They are: (1) appearance of honour, (2) confirmation of prophethood, (3) becoming like a contemporary of prophets, (4) motivation for worship and refraining from sin, (5) incentive for other righteous people.
These benefits are enumerated in the commentary.
4
Reflect on the overall purpose
Understand that the benefits connect the saint to the prophetic mission and encourage striving for higher spiritual ranks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكروا أن لا فائدة منها قلنا: وإذا ثبت بما ذكرنا من الدلائل أنها ثابتة فبعد ذلك جهلكم بجهة الحكمة لا يوجب بطلانها على ما مر تقرير هذا من قبل. ثم نقول : فائدته ظهور كرامته على الله تعالى عنده، وثبوت رسالة من أمن به من الرسل بما شاهد من نقض العادة، فيصير كأحد من كان في عصر الأنبياء في حق مشاهدة المعجزة، ومعاينة نقض العادة مع أن ذلك يصير مبعثه له على الاجتهاد في العبادات والاحتراس عن السيئات إبقاء لتلك المنزلة على نفسه، وحفظاً لتلك المرتبة الشريفة والمنزلة العلية عن التبدل والزوال، وتحريضا لمن أطلعه الله عليها من الصالحين على الجد والاجتهاد ليبلغ تلك الدرجة وتناله تلك المنزلة.
And what they mentioned that there is no benefit in it — we say: If it is established by the proofs we have mentioned that it is real, then your ignorance of the aspect of wisdom does not necessitate its invalidity, as the explanation of this has preceded. Then we say: Its benefit is the appearance of his honour [from Allah] with Allah Almighty upon him, and the confirmation of the prophethood of the prophet he believes in, by witnessing the breaking of custom. Thus, he becomes like one of those who were in the era of the prophets with respect to witnessing the miracle and seeing the breaking of custom. Moreover, that becomes an impetus for him to strive in worship and refrain from evil deeds, to preserve that station for himself and to protect that noble rank and high station from change and loss, and as an incentive for those whom Allah has informed about it among the righteous to strive and exert themselves to reach that degree and attain that station.
Source pages p. 783

Commentary
This passage is a response to the objection that karamat have no benefit. The author first states that even if the objector does not understand the wisdom, that does not invalidate the karamah. Then he explains the benefits: (1) For the wali himself, it shows Allah's honour towards him. (2) It confirms the prophethood of the prophet he follows, as the karamah is a miracle indirectly confirming that prophet. (3) The wali becomes like someone from the prophet's time witnessing miracles firsthand, strengthening his faith. (4) It motivates him to increase worship and avoid sins to maintain that rank. (5) It encourages other righteous people who learn of it to strive to attain such a station.

Key Terms
فائدة
كرامة
حكمة
معجزة
عبادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think karamat have no benefit and are therefore pointless or impossible.
Correction: Nasafi explains that karamat have multiple benefits, both for the saint and for the broader purpose of confirming prophethood and inspiring righteousness.

A) It proves the saint is self-sufficient.
B) It confirms the prophethood of the prophet the saint follows.
C) It allows the saint to sin without consequence.
D) It negates the need for worship.

Key Takeaway
Karamat benefit the saint by confirming their honour and the prophet's truth, motivating worship, and inspiring others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Or do you secretly wish for a sign to confirm your belief? What does that desire say about the strength of your certainty?

Distinguishing Ma'unah from Other Supernatural Events
Nasafi defines ma'unah as a breach of custom for common believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine assistance (ma'unah) is a type of supernatural event that can occur for ordinary believers, distinct from miracles of prophets (mu'jizah) and saints (karamah).

Core Idea
Not every miraculous event is a saint's miracle; some are divine help for common believers.

Imam Nasafi now turns to a category of supernatural events that are not confined to prophets or saints. He cites the people of knowledge to show that a breach of custom can happen even to an ordinary Muslim, serving as divine assistance (ma'unah) to rescue them from a trial. This distinction helps us understand the variety of miraculous phenomena in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and its literal translation. Notice the key terms: ma'unah, nāqiḍ al-'ādah, 'awāmm, miḥnah.
This passage is a single concise statement from the people of knowledge.
2
Identify the key terms
Look at each term: ma'unah (divine assistance), nāqiḍ al-'ādah (breach of custom), 'awāmm al-muslimīn (common Muslims), miḥnah (trial). Understand how they relate to the definition.
The term 'nāqiḍ al-'ādah' is the generic term for any supernatural event.
3
Reflect on the distinction
Consider how ma'unah differs from karamah (saint's miracle) and mu'jizah (prophet's miracle). Why is it important that ordinary believers can experience breaches of custom?
This helps avoid the misconception that every supernatural event is a sign of sanctity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل العلم بالحقائق إن ظهور الناقض للعادة ربما يكون من الفرط لواحد من عوام المسلمين، وتكون معونة له في التخلص عن محنة توجهت إليه.
And the people of knowledge of realities said: The appearance of a breach of custom may sometimes occur from an ordinary common Muslim, and it is a ma'unah (divine assistance) for him in escaping a trial that has befallen him.
Source pages p. 783

Commentary
This passage is a brief definition and explanation of ma'unah (divine assistance). The author cites the people of knowledge (ahl al-'ilm bil-haqa'iq) to clarify that not every miracle-like event (nāqiḍ al-'ādah) is a karamah. Sometimes such an event happens to an ordinary Muslim (not necessarily a saint) and serves as divine help to save him from a difficulty. This distinguishes ma'unah from karamah, which is specific to saints, and from mu'jizah, which is specific to prophets. The key point is that a breach of custom can occur for a non-saint as a form of divine aid.

Key Terms
معونة (ma'unah)
ناقض العادة (breach of custom)
عوام المسلمين (common Muslims)
محنة (trial)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All supernatural events are karamat (saintly miracles).
Correction: Some breaches of custom are ma'unah, which can happen to ordinary Muslims and are not signs of sanctity but divine help.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes ma'unah from karamah according to this passage?
A) Ma'unah only occurs for prophets.
B) Ma'unah can occur for ordinary common Muslims, while karamah is for saints.
C) Ma'unah is always concealed.
D) Ma'unah is never a breach of custom.

Key Takeaway
Divine assistance (ma'unah) is a breach of custom that occurs for ordinary Muslims as help from Allah in escaping trials.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, do you assume that any miraculous relief is a sign of your own sainthood, or can you accept that it might simply be Allah's ma'unah for you as an ordinary believer? What does this teach you about humility?
?
How does knowing that Allah grants ma'unah to ordinary Muslims change the way you view your own struggles? Are you quick to attribute your successes to your own efforts, or do you see them as divine assistance?
?
If ma'unah is a breach of custom for common believers, why do you think so many of us fail to recognize it in our lives? What barrier in your heart prevents you from seeing Allah's help as a gift rather than a coincidence?

Distinguishing Mu'jiza and Karama
Distinguishes mu'jiza from karama by claim, display, and protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key differences between a prophet's miracle (mu'jiza) and a saint's gift (karama), including the roles of claim, concealment, and divine protection.

Core Idea
The sign of a miracle is openness; the sign of a saintly gift is concealment.

The author begins by addressing a potential confusion: how can we tell a prophet's miracle from a saintly gift? He explains that the context of the claim, the behavior of the recipient, and the level of divine protection provide clear distinctions. This passage establishes the foundational criteria.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Read the passage and mark where mu'jiza and karama are described.
2
Notice the role of claim
Observe that mu'jiza requires a claim of prophethood, while karama does not.
3
Compare concealment vs. display
Note that the prophet displays his miracle, while the saint hides his gift.
4
Consider fear of istidraj
Understand why the saint fears his gift might be a trap.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: وكيف يؤدي ذلك إلى التباس الكرامة بالمعجزة، والمعجزة تظهر على أثر دعوى الرسالة، ولو ادعى الولي الرسالة لكفر من ساعته، وصار عدوا الله لا يظهر على يده نقض العادة البتة، ولو ادعى الولاية تسقط عنه الولاية عند دعواه إياها، وكذا صاحب المعجزة لا يكتم معجزته بل يظهرها، وصاحب الكرامة يجتهد في كتمانها ولا يركن في الأغلب إليها، ويخاف أنها من قبيل الاستدراج له دون الكرامة، ولو اطلع الله تعالى أحدًا من صالحي عباده على كرامة الولي لتشفع إليه الولي وطلب بغاية التضرع أن يكتم ذلك عليه ولا يفشيه خوفا من الاغترار لدى الاشتهار، وكذا صاحب المعجزة مأمون العاقبة معصوم عن التبديل والولي بخلافه. وما ذكروا أن لا فائدة منها قلنا: وإذا ثبت بما ذكرنا من الدلائل أنها ثابتة فبعد ذلك جهلكم بجهة الحكمة لا يوجب بطلانها على ما مر تقرير هذا من قبل. ثم نقول: فائدته ظهور كرامته على الله تعالى عنده، وثبوت رسالة من أمن به من الرسل بما شاهد من نقض العادة، فيصير كأحد من كان في عصر الأنبياء في حق مشاهدة المعجزة، ومعاينة نقض العادة مع أن ذلك يصير مبعثه له على الاجتهاد في العبادات والاحتراس عن السيئات إبقاء لتلك المنزلة على نفسه، وحفظا لتلك المرتبة الشريفة والمنزلة العلية عن التبدل والزوال، وتحريضا لمن أطلعه الله عليها من الصالحين على الجد والاجتهاد ليبلغ تلك الدرجة وتناله تلك المنزلة. وقال أهل العلم بالحقائق إن ظهور الناقض للعادة ربما يكون من الفرط لواحد من عوام المسلمين، وتكون معونة له في التخلص عن محنة توجهت إليه، ومكروه أقبل عليه، ويسمى ذلك معونة لا كرامة، وقد تظهر أيضا على يد المتأله وعلى يد الساحر عند انعدام دعوى النبوة، ولهذا ذكر محمد بن الحسن رواية عن أبي حنيفة - رحمهما الله - أن المؤخذ بمنزلة العنين وهو الذي أخذ بالسحر عن النساء ويكون ذلك إهانة لمن ظهر على يديه. وجاء من هذا أن الناقض للعادة على أنواع أربعة معجزة، وكرامة، ومعونة، وإهانة، والفرق بينها ما بينا.
Then we say: How does that lead to confusion between karama and mu'jiza? And mu'jiza appears as a result of the claim of prophethood. If a wali claimed prophethood, he would disbelieve immediately and become an enemy of Allah, and no violation of custom would ever appear at his hand. If he claimed walaya, his walaya falls from him upon his claim. Also, the possessor of a mu'jiza does not conceal his mu'jiza but rather displays it. The possessor of karama strives to conceal it and mostly does not rely upon it, and fears that it might be a form of istidraj (gradual leading to downfall) for him rather than a karama. If Allah Almighty informs any of His righteous servants about the karama of a wali, the wali would intercede and request with utmost supplication that He conceal it for him and not make it known, for fear of delusion upon fame. Likewise, the possessor of a mu'jiza is secure in outcome and protected from alteration, unlike the wali. And as for their claim that there is no benefit in it, we say: If it is established by the proofs we have mentioned that it is established, then your ignorance of the aspect of wisdom does not necessitate its invalidity, as has been explained previously. Then we say: Its benefit is the manifestation to him of his karama from Allah Almighty, and the confirmation of the prophethood of the prophet he believed in, by what he witnessed of violation of custom. Thus he becomes like one of those who were in the era of the prophets with respect to witnessing the mu'jiza and observing the violation of custom. Moreover, that becomes an impetus for him to strive in acts of worship and abstain from evil deeds in order to preserve that station for himself and guard that noble rank and lofty station from change and disappearance, and a motivation for those righteous ones whom Allah has informed of it to be serious and diligent in order to reach that degree and attain that station. And the people of knowledge of realities said: The appearance of a violation of custom might sometimes occur for an ordinary Muslim and be a ma'una (divine aid) for him to escape from a trial that befell him or a disliked thing that confronted him, and that is called ma'una, not karama. It may also appear at the hand of a claimant to divinity (mut'allah) and at the hand of a magician in the absence of a claim of prophethood. For this reason, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa—may Allah have mercy on them—that the one afflicted by magic (al-mu'khadh) is in the position of an impotent man, being one who is seized by magic from women, and that is an ihana (degradation) for the one at whose hand it appears. And from this it follows that the violations of custom are of four types: mu'jiza, karama, ma'una, and ihana, and the distinction between them is as we have explained.
Source pages p. 783

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification and distinction of four types of supernatural events (violations of custom) that can appear: mu'jiza (miracle of a prophet), karama (gift of honor for a saint/ wali), ma'una (divine aid for an ordinary believer), and ihana (degradation for an impostor or magician). The author first addresses an objection that these types might be confused. He explains that a mu'jiza always accompanies a claim of prophethood and is openly displayed, whereas a karama appears for a wali who does not claim prophethood; if the wali claimed prophethood he would become a disbeliever and no miracle would appear. The wali hides his karama and fears it might be a trap (istidraj). The possessor of a mu'jiza is divinely protected from alteration, while the wali is not. The author then refutes the objection that these events have no benefit, listing several benefits: they confirm God's honor for the wali, strengthen believers' faith in the prophethood of their prophet, motivate the wali to increase worship and avoid sins, and inspire others to strive for that rank. Next, he introduces ma'una as a sudden supernatural help for an ordinary Muslim in distress, and ihana as a supernatural event at the hand of a false claimant or magician, which degrades them. He cites a report from Abu Hanifa about a man afflicted by magic, which is considered ihana. The passage concludes by enumerating the four types and stating that the distinctions have been clarified.

Key Terms
المعجزة
الكرامة
الولي
الاستدراج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all supernatural events are miracles and cannot be distinguished.
Correction: The passage provides clear signs: a miracle is tied to a prophet's claim, openly displayed, and divinely protected; a saintly gift is hidden and feared as a possible trap.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes the behavior of the possessor of a mu'jiza from the possessor of a karama regarding display?
A) The possessor of mu'jiza hides it, while the possessor of karama shows it.
B) Both display openly.
C) The possessor of mu'jiza displays it openly, while the possessor of karama strives to conceal it.
D) The possessor of karama displays it after a claim.

Key Takeaway
A miracle is openly displayed by a prophet after a claim, while a saintly gift is concealed and feared as a possible trap.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been tempted to share a spiritual experience or good deed in order to be seen as pious? How does the saint's desperate effort to conceal his karama confront your own desire for recognition?
?
If you performed an act of worship and suddenly felt a special spiritual uplifting, would you interpret it as Allah's pleasure or fear that it might be istidraj? What does this lesson compel you to examine in your own heart?
?
Imagine you are the saint in this passage: Allah reveals your karama to others despite your request to hide it. Would your immediate reaction be fear or pride? Why does the passage insist that concealment is the only safe path?

The Benefits of Karama and Refuting Doubts
Lists the benefits of karama and refutes the objection of futility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the benefits of karama as explained by the author and why the objection of no benefit is invalid.

Core Idea
Karama confirms God's honor for the saint, strengthens faith, and motivates worship.

After clarifying the distinction, the author addresses an objection: what benefit is there in karama? He provides several benefits that show karama's importance for the saint, the believer, and the wider community. This passage reinforces the value of these divine gifts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the objection
Find where the author responds to the claim that karama has no benefit.
2
List the benefits
Identify the three benefits mentioned: manifestation of honor, confirmation of prophethood, and motivation for worship.
3
Understand the refutation
Note that ignorance of wisdom does not negate existence.
4
Reflect on motivation
See how these benefits encourage both the saint and others to strive.
