Ma'una, Ihana, and the Four Types of Violations of Custom
Introduces ma'una and ihana, then enumerates all four types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concepts of ma'una and ihana as additional types of violations of custom, and how they complete the fourfold classification.

Core Idea
Not all violations of custom are miracles or saintly gifts; some are divine aid for the ordinary believer or degradation for the impostor.

The author completes the classification by introducing two more categories: ma'una, a sudden divine aid for an ordinary Muslim in distress, and ihana, a supernatural event that degrades a magician or false claimant. With these, he establishes a complete four-type system of violations of custom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read about ma'una occurring for an ordinary Muslim.
2
Identify ihana
Find the case of the magician or false claimant where the event degrades them.
3
Understand the final enumeration
Note that the author concludes with four types.
4
Review the distinctions
Summarize the key signs for each type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: وكيف يؤدي ذلك إلى التباس الكرامة بالمعجزة، والمعجزة تظهر على أثر دعوى الرسالة، ولو ادعى الولي الرسالة لكفر من ساعته، وصار عدوا الله لا يظهر على يده نقض العادة البتة، ولو ادعى الولاية تسقط عنه الولاية عند دعواه إياها، وكذا صاحب المعجزة لا يكتم معجزته بل يظهرها، وصاحب الكرامة يجتهد في كتمانها ولا يركن في الأغلب إليها، ويخاف أنها من قبيل الاستدراج له دون الكرامة، ولو اطلع الله تعالى أحدًا من صالحي عباده على كرامة الولي لتشفع إليه الولي وطلب بغاية التضرع أن يكتم ذلك عليه ولا يفشيه خوفا من الاغترار لدى الاشتهار، وكذا صاحب المعجزة مأمون العاقبة معصوم عن التبديل والولي بخلافه. وما ذكروا أن لا فائدة منها قلنا: وإذا ثبت بما ذكرنا من الدلائل أنها ثابتة فبعد ذلك جهلكم بجهة الحكمة لا يوجب بطلانها على ما مر تقرير هذا من قبل. ثم نقول: فائدته ظهور كرامته على الله تعالى عنده، وثبوت رسالة من أمن به من الرسل بما شاهد من نقض العادة، فيصير كأحد من كان في عصر الأنبياء في حق مشاهدة المعجزة، ومعاينة نقض العادة مع أن ذلك يصير مبعثه له على الاجتهاد في العبادات والاحتراس عن السيئات إبقاء لتلك المنزلة على نفسه، وحفظا لتلك المرتبة الشريفة والمنزلة العلية عن التبدل والزوال، وتحريضا لمن أطلعه الله عليها من الصالحين على الجد والاجتهاد ليبلغ تلك الدرجة وتناله تلك المنزلة. وقال أهل العلم بالحقائق إن ظهور الناقض للعادة ربما يكون من الفرط لواحد من عوام المسلمين، وتكون معونة له في التخلص عن محنة توجهت إليه، ومكروه أقبل عليه، ويسمى ذلك معونة لا كرامة، وقد تظهر أيضا على يد المتأله وعلى يد الساحر عند انعدام دعوى النبوة، ولهذا ذكر محمد بن الحسن رواية عن أبي حنيفة - رحمهما الله - أن المؤخذ بمنزلة العنين وهو الذي أخذ بالسحر عن النساء ويكون ذلك إهانة لمن ظهر على يديه. وجاء من هذا أن الناقض للعادة على أنواع أربعة معجزة، وكرامة، ومعونة، وإهانة، والفرق بينها ما بينا.
Then we say: How does that lead to confusion between karama and mu'jiza? And mu'jiza appears as a result of the claim of prophethood. If a wali claimed prophethood, he would disbelieve immediately and become an enemy of Allah, and no violation of custom would ever appear at his hand. If he claimed walaya, his walaya falls from him upon his claim. Also, the possessor of a mu'jiza does not conceal his mu'jiza but rather displays it. The possessor of karama strives to conceal it and mostly does not rely upon it, and fears that it might be a form of istidraj (gradual leading to downfall) for him rather than a karama. If Allah Almighty informs any of His righteous servants about the karama of a wali, the wali would intercede and request with utmost supplication that He conceal it for him and not make it known, for fear of delusion upon fame. Likewise, the possessor of a mu'jiza is secure in outcome and protected from alteration, unlike the wali. And as for their claim that there is no benefit in it, we say: If it is established by the proofs we have mentioned that it is established, then your ignorance of the aspect of wisdom does not necessitate its invalidity, as has been explained previously. Then we say: Its benefit is the manifestation to him of his karama from Allah Almighty, and the confirmation of the prophethood of the prophet he believed in, by what he witnessed of violation of custom. Thus he becomes like one of those who were in the era of the prophets with respect to witnessing the mu'jiza and observing the violation of custom. Moreover, that becomes an impetus for him to strive in acts of worship and abstain from evil deeds in order to preserve that station for himself and guard that noble rank and lofty station from change and disappearance, and a motivation for those righteous ones whom Allah has informed of it to be serious and diligent in order to reach that degree and attain that station. And the people of knowledge of realities said: The appearance of a violation of custom might sometimes occur for an ordinary Muslim and be a ma'una (divine aid) for him to escape from a trial that befell him or a disliked thing that confronted him, and that is called ma'una, not karama. It may also appear at the hand of a claimant to divinity (mut'allah) and at the hand of a magician in the absence of a claim of prophethood. For this reason, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa—may Allah have mercy on them—that the one afflicted by magic (al-mu'khadh) is in the position of an impotent man, being one who is seized by magic from women, and that is an ihana (degradation) for the one at whose hand it appears. And from this it follows that the violations of custom are of four types: mu'jiza, karama, ma'una, and ihana, and the distinction between them is as we have explained.
Source pages p. 783

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification and distinction of four types of supernatural events (violations of custom) that can appear: mu'jiza (miracle of a prophet), karama (gift of honor for a saint/ wali), ma'una (divine aid for an ordinary believer), and ihana (degradation for an impostor or magician). The author first addresses an objection that these types might be confused. He explains that a mu'jiza always accompanies a claim of prophethood and is openly displayed, whereas a karama appears for a wali who does not claim prophethood; if the wali claimed prophethood he would become a disbeliever and no miracle would appear. The wali hides his karama and fears it might be a trap (istidraj). The possessor of a mu'jiza is divinely protected from alteration, while the wali is not. The author then refutes the objection that these events have no benefit, listing several benefits: they confirm God's honor for the wali, strengthen believers' faith in the prophethood of their prophet, motivate the wali to increase worship and avoid sins, and inspire others to strive for that rank. Next, he introduces ma'una as a sudden supernatural help for an ordinary Muslim in distress, and ihana as a supernatural event at the hand of a false claimant or magician, which degrades them. He cites a report from Abu Hanifa about a man afflicted by magic, which is considered ihana. The passage concludes by enumerating the four types and stating that the distinctions have been clarified.

Key Terms
المعونة
الإهانة
المتأله
الساحر
نقض العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all supernatural events are either miracles or saintly gifts.
Correction: The passage shows that there are also divine aid for ordinary people and degradation for impostors.

Checkpoint
What is the name for a violation of custom that occurs for an ordinary Muslim to help him out of a trial?
A) Mu'jiza
B) Karama
C) Ma'una
D) Ihana

Key Takeaway
Violations of custom are of four types: mu'jiza, karama, ma'una, and ihana, each with specific contexts and purposes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Has there been a moment in your life when you received unexpected help (ma'una) from Allah in a difficult situation, and you either took it for granted or attributed it to your own cleverness? How will you train yourself to recognize such moments as divine aid and respond with gratitude?
?
This lesson teaches that even a magician can perform supernatural acts—but those acts are a source of degradation (ihana) for him. Does this make you more cautious about being impressed by people who display extraordinary powers? How will you use this knowledge to anchor your faith in the clear proofs of revelation rather than fleeting wonders?
?
Imagine you witness a supernatural event from a person who claims to be a saint. According to this lesson, it could be karama or just ma'una—but how would you discern? What attitude should you cultivate in your heart toward such events so that you neither blindly reject nor arrogantly claim? Commit to one practical step to keep your focus on the Giver, not the gift.

Miracles
beginner
5 min
The Four Types of Breaks in Custom
Al-Nasafi classifies the four types of breaks in custom and clarifies their signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four types of divine breaks in natural custom and how they are distinguished by the status of the person on whose hands they appear.

Core Idea
Not all miraculous events are miracles; they reveal the spiritual rank of the person.

Imam al-Nasafi completes his discussion of extraordinary events by categorizing them into four distinct types. Each type corresponds to a specific spiritual status: prophets receive miracles, saints receive graces, pious believers receive assistance, and impostors receive humiliation. This passage establishes the criteria for distinguishing these events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the flow from a specific example to the general classification.
2
Identify the four types
Find the four terms listed for the breaks in custom: mu'jizah, karamah, ma'unah, and ihana. Note the context that precedes each.
The distinction depends on the person: prophet, saint, pious believer, or impostor.
3
Understand the distinctions
The passage explains that a break in custom is called a miracle for a prophet, a grace for a saint, assistance for a believer, and humiliation for an impostor. Ask yourself why the same type of event can have different names.
The key is the person's spiritual state and claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومكروه أقبل عليه، ويسمى ذلك معونة لا كرامة، وقد تظهر أيضا على يد المتأله وعلى يد الساحر عند انعدام دعوى النبوة، ولهذا ذكر محمد بن الحسن رواية عن أبي حنيفة رحمهما الله أن المؤخذ بمنزلة العنين وهو الذي أخذ بالسحر عن النساء ويكون ذلك إهانة لمن ظهر على يديه. وجاء من هذا أن الناقض للعادة على أنواع أربعة معجزة، وكرامة، ومعونة، وإهانة، والفرق بينها ما بينا.
And something disliked occurs before him, and that is called assistance not grace, and it may also appear on the hand of the claimant to divinity and on the hand of the sorcerer when there is no claim of prophethood, and for this reason Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on them, that the one afflicted is like the impotent who is bewitched from women, and that is a humiliation for the one on whose hand it appears. And from this comes that the breaker of custom is of four types: miracle, grace, assistance, and humiliation, and the distinction between them is what we have explained.
Source pages p. 784

Commentary
This passage classifies events that break natural custom into four categories. The author begins by discussing a specific case: an event that is disliked (makruh) yet occurs as an assistance (ma‘unah) to a believer, distinguishing it from a grace (karamah) which is for a saint. He then notes that such events can also appear on the hand of a false claimant to divinity (muta’allih) or a sorcerer when no prophethood is claimed, citing a narration from Abu Hanifa that such occurrences are a humiliation (ihānah) for the person. From this, the author concludes that there are four types: miracle (mu‘jizah) for prophets, grace (karamah) for saints, assistance (ma‘unah) for pious believers, and humiliation (ihānah) for impostors. The distinction is based on the condition of the person on whose hands the event occurs.

Key Terms
الناقض للعادة
معجزة
كرامة
معونة
إهانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All supernatural events are miracles (mu'jizah).
Correction: The passage teaches that there are four types: miracles for prophets, graces for saints, assistance for believers, and humiliation for impostors. The same event can be different depending on the person.

Checkpoint
Which type of break in custom appears on the hand of a righteous saint who does not claim prophethood?
A) Miracle (معجزة)
B) Grace (كرامة)
C) Assistance (معونة)
D) Humiliation (إهانة)

Key Takeaway
The four types of breaks in custom—miracle, grace, assistance, and humiliation—are distinguished by the spiritual status of the person on whose hands they occur, not by the event itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever witnessed or heard of an event that seemed to break the usual pattern of nature? How did you respond to it? Did you immediately assume it was a miracle? Examine your heart: are you looking for signs in events to affirm your faith, or are you content with the clarity of revelation? Commit to seeking the truth about such events by referring to the criteria taught in this lesson.
?
If a supernatural event occurred in your life, which of the four types would you hope it to be? Why? What does that preference reveal about your spiritual ambition? Are you seeking honor from people or from Allah? Repent if your intention is not purely for Allah's sake.
?
The passage mentions that some events are humiliations for impostors. In your own life, are there abilities or successes that you attribute to yourself rather than to Allah? Could any of your accomplishments actually be a test or a humiliation? Reflect on the means through which you achieve things and ask Allah to make you reliant on Him alone.
